Washing Braided Hair in Ghusl: Men vs. Women
Ruling with proof: distinguishing obligation for men vs. women in ghusl.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on washing braided hair in ghusl for men and women, explain the proof from the hadith of Umm Salamah, and distinguish between the obligations for each gender.

Core Idea
For men, braided hair must be fully wetted; for women, only the roots need to be wet — a concession based on hardship.

In this lesson, we examine a specific point from the chapter of ghusl: how to handle braided hair. The Hanafi school makes a clear distinction between men and women. Men must undo their braids to ensure every strand is washed, while women are excused from undoing their braids — as long as water reaches the roots. This concession, derived from a direct prophetic hadith, reflects the principle of removing hardship in worship.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Recognize that the text rules on the obligation to wash braided hair during ghusl. For men, washing the braided hair itself is fard; for women, only reaching the roots is fard.
The ruling is part of the obligatory elements (fara'id) of ghusl.
2
Locate the dalil
The primary proof is the hadith of Umm Salamah in Sahih Muslim and Sunan Abi Dawud. The author also cites a narration from Aishah about reaching the roots.
The hadith is ahad but its meaning is clear.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet (ﷺ) explicitly told Umm Salamah she need not undo her braids; three handfuls of water over the head suffice. This shows that wetting the roots is sufficient for women.
The command 'لا' (no) indicates a concession, not an absolute prohibition.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Some Shafi'i scholars hold that women must also wet the entire braided hair. The Hanafi school maintains the concession based on hardship and the explicit hadith.
The difference is rooted in how the hadith is interpreted and the weight given to hardship.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The Hanafi position is mufta bihi because it relies on a clear, specific prophetic permission and is consistent with the principle of istihsan alleviating difficulty.
Later Hanafi masters reaffirm this as the relied-upon position.

تشریح : مرد کا گوندھا ہوا بال ہو تو اس گوندھے ہوئے بال میں پانی پہنچانا ضروری ہے اور بال کی جڑوں میں بھی پانی پہنچانا ضروری ہے چاہے جوڑے کو کھول کر پانی پہنچانا پڑے۔ البتہ عورت کا جوڑا بندھا ہوا ہو تو گوندھے ہوئے بالوں میں پانی پہنچانا ضروری نہیں ہے ، صرف بال کی جڑوں میں پانی پہنچانا ضروری ہے، کیونکہ عورت کی بار بار کی مجبوری کی وجہ سے حدیث موجود ہے۔
وجه : (۱) آیت کے اعتبار سے ہر ہر بال کو دھونا ضروری ہے، چنانچہ مرد کے بال کے بارے میں یہی مسئلہ ہے، البتہ عورت کو چونکہ مجبوری ہے اس لئے وہ جوڑے کو نہ بھی بھیگائے تو جائز ہے ۔ (۲) حدیث یہ ہے۔ عن ام سـلـمـة قــالـت قلـت یـا رسول الله علم انى امرأة اشد ضفر رأسى افأنقضه لغسل الجنابة ؟قال لا ، انما يكفيك ان تحثی علی رأسك ثلاث حثيات ثم تفیضین علیك الماء فتطهرين (مسلم شریف، باب حکم ضفائر المغتسلة ص ۱۴۶ نمبر ۱۳۳۰ ۷۴۴ را بودا و دشریف، باب المرأة هل تنقض شعرها عند الغسل نمبر (۲۵) (۳) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ عورت کو بھی بال کی جڑ میں پانی

فتدلكه دلكا شديدا حتى تبلغ شؤن رأسها (مسلم شریف، باب استعمال المغتسلة من الحيض فرصة من مسلك في موضع الدم ص ۱۴۷، نمبر ۷۵۰٫۳۳۲ ) اس حدیث سے ثابت ہوا کہ پانی بالوں کی جڑوں کے اندر پہنچانا ضروری ہے تب غسل ہوگا ۔ اگر جوڑا نہیں کھولا اور پانی جڑ تک نہیں پہنچا تو عورتوں کا غسل نہیں ہوگا۔
لغت : مضفور: ضفر سے مشتق ہے، جوڑا باندھنا۔ سری سرایت کرنا۔ اصول : جڑ ۔ بال کی جڑ۔ بشرۃ: کھال۔
And the inside of the braided hair of a man absolutely (must be washed), but not the braided hair of a woman if water reaches its roots. He would run his fingers through his hair until he saw that he had reached the skin or had cleaned the skin, then he would pour water over his head three times, and if there was an excess, he would pour it over himself. (Abu Dawud, Bab fi al-Ghusl min al-Janabah, p. 25, no. 242) This hadith indicates that water reaches the roots of the hair and the skin, from which it can be inferred that water must reach the prepuce, inside the navel, and inside a piercing. (3) And from the practice of a Companion: He would pour water into his eyes and insert his finger into his navel when performing ghusl from janabah. (Sunan al-Bayhaqi, Bab Nafkh al-Ma' fi al-'Aynayn wa Idkhal al-Isba' fi al-Surrah, vol. 1, p. 273, no. 837) This effect shows that he would put water in the navel.
Vocabulary: Qulfa: the skin cut during circumcision. 'Usr: difficulty. Surrah: navel. Thaqb: piercing. Munjadhim: closed.
Translation: (169) [7] And the washing of a man's braided hair in all cases, but not a woman's braided hair, provided water reaches its roots.
Explanation: If a man has braided hair, it is necessary to wet the braided hair itself and also to reach the roots of the hair, even if it requires untying the braids. As for a woman with braided hair, it is not necessary to wet the braided hair itself; only reaching the roots is required, due to a hadith excusing women's hardship.
Evidence: (1) Based on the verse, every hair must be washed; this applies to men. For women, due to hardship, it is permissible not to wet the braids. (2) The hadith: Umm Salamah said: I asked, O Messenger of Allah, I am a woman who strongly braids her hair – shall I undo it for ghusl from janabah? He said: No, it suffices you to pour three handfuls of water over your head, then pour water over yourself and become purified. (Muslim, Bab Hukm Dha'ifir al-Mughtasilah, p. 146, no. 1330; Abu Dawud, Bab al-Mar'ah Hal Tanqud Sha'raha 'ind al-Ghusl, no. 251) (3) This hadith shows that water must reach the roots of a woman's hair. From Aishah: Asma asked the Prophet about ghusl from menstruation... then pour water over her head and rub it vigorously until water reaches the roots of her hair. (Muslim, Bab Istikhdam al-Mughtasilah min al-Hayd Firasha min Muskki fi Mowdi' al-Dam, p. 147, no. 750) This hadith establishes that water must reach the roots of the hair for ghusl to be valid. If the braids are not untied and water does not reach the roots, women's ghusl is not valid.
Vocabulary: Mudhfar: derived from dafr, to braid. Sariya: to penetrate. Usul: roots (of hair). Bushrah: skin.
Source pages p. 139

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding braided hair during ghusl, distinguishing between men and women. The matn states: 'And the inside of the braided hair of a man absolutely (must be washed), but not the braided hair of a woman if water reaches its roots.' The Urdu commentary explains that for a man, braided hair must be undone to ensure water reaches both the braids and the roots (usul). For a woman, it is sufficient if water reaches the roots; she need not undo her braids due to the hardship of frequent ghusl (e.g., after menstruation or postpartum). The author provides hadith proofs: First, a hadith from Umm Salamah where the Prophet explicitly said she need not undo her braids; pouring three handfuls of water over the head is sufficient if water reaches the roots. Second, from Aishah regarding ghusl from menses, emphasizing that water must reach the roots of the hair. The author also cites the practice of Ibn Umar as evidence for washing the navel and eyes. The key legal point is that the obligation is to wet the roots of the hair; for men, the braids are an obstacle that must be removed, but for women, due to the concession of hardship, the braids themselves need not be wetted. This is a clear example of istihsan (juristic preference) in the Hanafi school, alleviating women's difficulty. The authority weight from the matn is Zahir al-Riwayah.

Key Terms
مضفور (mudhfar): Braided or plaited hair; the text distinguishes between a man's and woman's braids.
أصول الشعر (usul al-sha'r): The roots of the hair where it meets the scalp; water must reach them for ghusl to be valid.
ضفر (dafr): The act of braiding hair; the text derives mudhfar from it.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling for a man with braided hair performing ghusl?
A) He may keep his braids if water reaches the roots.
B) He must undo his braids to ensure water reaches both the braids and the roots.
C) He is excused from washing his hair altogether if braided.
D) He must wash only the roots, not the braids themselves.

Key Takeaway
In ghusl, men must fully wet braided hair, while women need only reach the roots—a concession based on the hadith of Umm Salamah to alleviate hardship.

Taharah — Purification

Washing Braided Hair in Ghusl: Men vs Women
Ruling on washing braided hair in ghusl for men and women.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on washing braided hair in ghusl for men and women, and explain the hadith evidence that supports the differentiation.

Core Idea
Water must reach the hair roots for valid ghusl, but women need not undo braids due to the Prophet's explicit concession.

This passage addresses a common practical question: when a person has braided hair, must they undo it for ghusl? The Hanafi school differentiates between men and women based on clear hadith evidence. Understanding this ruling helps avoid undue hardship while fulfilling the obligation of purification.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is being ruled upon? The obligation of washing hair during ghusl when the hair is braided. Note the ruling: for men, washing braided hair is fard; for women, only reaching the roots is fard.
The distinction hinges on the gender-specific hardship.
2
Locate the primary dalil
The hadith of Umm Salamah: she asked the Prophet ﷺ about undoing her tight braid for ghusl, and he replied, 'No, it is sufficient for you to pour three handfuls on your head...' This is the core evidence for women's concession.
The hadith is found in Muslim and Abu Dawud.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet's explicit 'لا' (no) indicates undoing braids is not required. The phrase 'انما يكفيك' (only suffices you) and 'تحثي على رأسك' (pour on your head) imply that pouring water on the head is enough, provided water reaches the roots.
This hadith only addresses women; men are not covered by this concession.
4
Examine the supporting dalil
The hadith of Aisha about Asma's question on ghusl from menstruation: the Prophet taught to pour water on the head and rub vigorously until water reaches the roots. This confirms that reaching the roots is obligatory for all.
This hadith reinforces that roots must become wet; it does not exempt women from root wetness.
5
Apply the ruling to both genders
For men, the general obligation to wash every hair applies fully, so braided hair must be washed by ensuring water reaches both the braid and the roots. For women, only the roots need water; the braids themselves need not be loosened.
This is mufta bihi in the Hanafi school.

Section on the Obligations of Ghusl (169) And the washing of the braided hair of a man absolutely, not the braided hair of a woman, if water penetrates to its roots. So he should sift his hair until he sees that it has reached the skin or cleansed the skin, then pour over his head three times. If there is excess, pour it over him. (Abu Dawud Sharif, Bab fi al-Ghusl min al-Janabah, p. 25, no. 242) In this hadith he would make water reach the roots of the hair, and make water reach the skin. From this can be deduced that the foreskin, inside the navel, and inside the openings should be reached by water. (3) In this action of a Companion he would make water reach inside the navel and inside the eyes. From Ibn Umar he said: When he performed ghusl from janabah he would sprinkle water in his eyes and insert his finger into his navel (Sunan Bayhaqi, Bab Nafkh al-Ma' fi al-'Aynayn wa Idkhal al-Isba' fi al-Surrah, vol. 1 p. 273, no. 837). In this athar he would pour water into the navel. Lexicon: Qulfah: the skin cut during circumcision. 'Usr: difficulty. Surrah: navel. Thaqb: opening. Mundamm: joined. Translation: (169) [7] And washing the braided hair of a man absolutely, not the braided hair of a woman, when water reaches its roots. Explanation: If a man has braided hair, it is obligatory to make water reach within the braided hair and also to the roots of the hair, even if it requires loosening the braid. As for a woman, if she has braided hair, it is not obligatory to make water reach within the braided hair; it is only obligatory to make water reach the roots of the hair, because of the hadith due to woman's frequent hardship. Reasoning: (1) Based on the verse, it is obligatory to wash every single hair; thus for a man's hair this is the ruling. However, since a woman has hardship, it is permissible for her not to wet the braid. (2) The hadith: Umm Salamah said: I said, O Messenger of Allah, I am a woman who ties her hair tightly; should I undo it for ghusl from janabah? He said: No, it is sufficient for you to pour three handfuls on your head, then pour water over yourself and you will be purified. (Muslim Sharif, Bab Hukm Dafa'ir al-Mughtasilah, p. 146, no. 1330/744; Abu Dawud Sharif, Bab al-Mar'ah Hal Tanqud Sha'raha 'inda al-Ghusl, no. 25) (3) In this hadith it is necessary for a woman to make water reach the roots of the hair. From Aisha: Asma asked the Prophet about ghusl from menstruation... then pour water on her head and rub it vigorously until water reaches the roots of her head (Muslim Sharif, Bab Isti'mal al-Mughtasilah min al-Hayd Furşah min Muslik fi Mowdi' al-Dam, p. 147, no. 750/332). This hadith proves that making water reach the roots of the hair is obligatory; then ghusl will be valid. If the braid is not loosened and water does not reach the roots, the ghusl of women will not be valid. Lexicon: Mudhfour: derived from dafr, tying a braid. Yaseeri: penetrating. Usool: roots. Bushrah: skin.
Source pages p. 139

Commentary
This passage deals with the obligation (fard) of washing the hair during ghusl, specifically when the hair is braided. The author states that a man must wash his braided hair completely, ensuring water reaches the roots. For a woman, however, if water reaches the roots, the braided part need not be loosened and washed; it is sufficient that water reaches the roots. The proof is a hadith where Umm Salamah asked whether she needed to undo her tight braid for ghusl, and the Prophet ﷺ replied that three handfuls poured over the head suffice. Another hadith from Aisha emphasizes that water must reach the roots of the hair. The commentary explains that the general obligation to wash every hair (based on the Quranic command 'fa-ighsilu wujuhakum' extended to the entire body) applies to men fully, but women are given a concession due to hardship. Further, the author mentions that from the hadith of Abu Dawud, one can deduce that the foreskin, navel, and openings must have water reach them—this is also part of the obligation.

Key Terms
مضفور (mudhfour): Braided hair; hair that is tied or plaited.
قلفة (qulfah): The foreskin; the skin cut during circumcision.
سرت (surrah): The navel; the belly button.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling for a woman with braided hair performing ghusl?
A) She must undo all braids and wash every strand.
B) She must ensure water reaches the roots, and she may leave the braids tied.
C) She must cut off her braids before ghusl.
D) She does not need to wash her hair at all.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, for ghusl, men must wash their braided hair thoroughly, while women only need water to reach the roots of their hair, based on the explicit prophetic concession.

Obligatory Acts in Ghusl: Skin Under Facial Hair and External Private Parts
Ruling with proof from hadith and qiyas

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the four fard acts in ghusl related to facial hair and private parts and explain the evidence from hadith and qiyas.

Core Idea
In ghusl, washing the skin under facial hair and the external private part is fard, not just sunnah.

Although this passage appears under the heading 'Section on the Sunnahs of Ghusl,' the rulings for items (170) and (171) are actually obligations (fard). The text clarifies that the skin of the beard, mustache, and eyebrows must be washed – water must reach the skin. Similarly, the external private part must be washed, but not the internal. The proof comes from the practice of the Prophet ﷺ, and by qiyas, women also must wash their external private part. This lesson examines the ruling, evidence, and a minor cross-madhhab difference.

Guided Path
1
Identify the acts and their ruling
From the text, recognize that washing the skin of beard, mustache, eyebrows, and the external private part are ruled as fard (obligatory) in ghusl.
Note that the passage title says 'Sunnah' but the commentary explicitly states these are fard.
2
Locate the dalil (evidence)
The text cites hadith from Aisha and Maymunah (RA) describing the Prophet's ghusl practice. Identify that the Prophet washed his private part, indicating obligation.
The hadith are from Abu Dawud and Tirmidhi – ahad, but accepted.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah (how the proof shows the ruling)
The Prophet's consistent action of washing the private part is a model (fi'l) that indicates obligation in Hanafi usul. Similarly, the requirement to reach the roots of head hair (from earlier) is extended by qiyas to the skin under facial hair.
The text mentions qiyas for women – extending the same ruling.
4
Note the scope and boundaries
Only the external private part is fard; the internal part (inside the body) is not required. For facial hair, water must reach the skin, not just the hair.
This applies to both men and women.
5
Acknowledge cross-madhhab difference
Some schools consider washing the skin under thin hair as sunnah, not fard. The Hanafi position is fard based on the principle that water must reach the skin.
This difference affects validity: missing a fard invalidates ghusl, missing a sunnah does not.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل (۱۷۰) و بشرة اللحية وبشرة الشارب والحاجب (۱۷۱) والفرج الخارج. فصل : (يسن في الاغتسال اثنا عشر شيئا. ترجمه : (۱۷۰) [۸] اور ڈاڑھی کی کھال ۔ [9] اور مونچھ کی کھال ۔ [۱۰] اور ابرو کی کھال ۔ تشریح : او پر حدیث میں آیا کہ سر کے بال کی جڑ میں پانی پہنچانا ضروری ہے، اسی حدیث سے استدلال کرتے ہوئے یہ مسئلہ ہے کہ ڈاڑھی اور مونچھ اور ابرو کی کھال میں پانی پہنچانا فرض ہے۔ ترجمه : (۱۷۱) [1] اور فرج خارج کا دھونا فرض ہے] تشریح : فرج داخل کا حصہ جسم کے اندر کا حصہ ہے اس لئے اس میں پانی پہچانا فرض نہیں ہے ، اور فرج خارج باہر کا حصہ ہے اس لئے اس کو دھونا فرض ہے۔ وجه : (۱) عن عائشة قالت كان رسول الله صلى الله عليه اذا اغتسل من الجنابة .... ثم اتفقا فيغسل فرجه ، و قال مسدد : يفرغ على شماله ـ و ربما كنت عن الفرج - ابوداود شریف، باب فی الغسل من الجنابة ، ص ۴۵ ، نمبر ۲۴۲ ) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ فرج دھوتے تھے ، اسی پر قیاس کر کے عورت پر فرج خارج کا دھونا فرض ہوگا ۔ (۲) اس حدیث میں بھی ہے۔ اخبرنـا ابـن عبـاس عن خالته ميمونة .... ثم صب على فرجه فغسل فرجه بشماله ، ثم ضرب بيده الارض فغسلها - (ابوداود شریف، باب فی الغسل من الجنابة ، ص ۴۵، نمبر ۲۴۵ / / ترمذی شریف، باب ما جاء فی الغسل من الجنابۃ ص ۲۸، نمبر ۱۰۳) اس حدیث میں بھی ہے کہ آپ فرج دھویا کرتے تھے۔
Section (170) And the skin of the beard, the skin of the mustache, and the eyebrow. (171) And the external private part. Section: (Twelve things are sunnah in ghusl.) Translation: (170) [8] And the skin of the beard. [9] And the skin of the mustache. [10] And the skin of the eyebrow. Explanation: Above in the hadith it came that it is necessary to make water reach the roots of the hair of the head. Using that same hadith as evidence, the ruling is that making water reach the skin of the beard, mustache, and eyebrow is fard. Translation: (171) [1] And washing the external private part is fard. Explanation: The internal private part is part of the inside of the body, so making water reach it is not fard. The external private part is the outer part, so washing it is fard. Reasoning: (1) From Aisha, she said: The Messenger of Allah used to, when he performed ghusl from janabah... then they agreed: he would wash his private part. And Musaddad said: he would pour water on his left hand and sometimes on the private part. (Abu Dawud Sharif, Bab fi al-Ghusl min al-Janabah, p. 45, no. 242) In this hadith he used to wash the private part. By qiyas, washing the external private part is fard for women as well. (2) Also in this hadith: Ibn Abbas informed us from his aunt Maymunah... then he poured water on his private part and washed it with his left hand, then struck his hand on the ground and washed it. (Abu Dawud Sharif, Bab fi al-Ghusl min al-Janabah, p. 45, no. 245; Tirmidhi Sharif, Bab ma Ja' fi al-Ghusl min al-Janabah, p. 28, no. 103) In this hadith he used to wash the private part.
Source pages p. 140

Commentary
Although the heading says 'Section on the Sunnahs of Ghusl,' the rulings in numbers (170) and (171) are actually obligations (fard), as the commentary clarifies. The text states that it is obligatory to wash the skin of the beard, mustache, and eyebrows because water must reach the skin under the hair. This is derived from the same principle that water must reach the roots of head hair. For the private parts, it is obligatory to wash only the external area; the internal part (inside the body) is not required. The proof comes from the practice of the Prophet ﷺ, who would wash his private part during ghusl. This ruling applies to both men and women; for women, the external private part is the outer labia. The text notes that the list of twelve sunnahs (mentioned at the beginning of the section) is not elaborated here; only these rulings are discussed.

Key Terms
الفرج الخارج (al-farj al-kharij): The external private part; the visible outer genitalia.
بشرة اللحية (bushrat al-lihyah): The skin under the beard.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on washing the external private part during ghusl?
A) It is sunnah, but not obligatory.
B) It is fard for men only, not women.
C) It is fard for both men and women.
D) It is not required as long as water flows over the body.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi ghusl, it is fard to wash the skin under facial hair and the external private part; missing any invalidates the ghusl.

Sunnahs of Ghusl and Their Prophetic Proofs
Lists sunnah acts of ghusl with hadith evidence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the sunnah acts of ghusl and explain their evidence from the hadith of Aisha and Maimuna.

Core Idea
Following the Prophet's example in ghusl is sunnah; washing impurity first is established by his practice.

Ghusl is a fundamental act of purification, and while its obligatory elements are established in the Quran and Sunnah, the Prophet's detailed practice provides a model of recommended acts that enhance its completeness. This lesson examines the sunnah acts listed in the Thamaratun Najah text, along with the hadith proofs from Aisha and Maimuna that establish their status as sunnah rather than fard. Understanding this distinction helps the Muslim perform ghusl in the most perfect manner.

Guided Path
1
Identify the acts and their hukm
Read the Arabic text and locate the phrase 'يسن في الاغتسال اثنا عشر شيئا' (twelve things are sunnah in ghusl). The passage lists only the first few: basmalah, intention, washing hands to wrists, and washing impurity. Note the hukm level: sunnah (recommended), not fard or wajib.
The Hanafi school defines sunnah as an act that carries reward for doing and slight dislike (makruh tanzihi) for leaving, unlike wajib which requires compensation.
2
Locate the dalil (proof)
The author provides two hadith: from Aisha and Maimuna. Identify these as the proofs for the sunnah acts, particularly washing the private part and impurity first. The hadith describe the Prophet's exact sequence.
These are ahad hadith, but their content is consistent with the Prophet's established practice (sunnah fi'liyya).
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah (how the proof indicates sunnah)
The Prophet's actions are a model (uswa hasana) for the community. His doing of these acts consistently indicates that they are recommended, not obligatory. The absence of any command to do them makes them sunnah, not fard.
In Hanafi usul, the Prophet's action (fi'l) indicates ibaha (permissibility) or sunnah unless accompanied by evidence of obligation.
4
Note the fard clarification accompanying the sunnah
Before listing the sunnahs, the text mentions 'بشرة اللحية وبشرة الشارب والحاجب والفرج الخارج' (the skin of the beard, mustache, eyebrow, and external private part). This clarifies that water must reach these areas; it is fard, not sunnah. This distinction helps avoid confusion.
This fard reminder ensures the student does not mistakenly think covering these areas is only sunnah.
5
Evaluate the ikhtilaf (cross-madhhab difference)
The hanafi_position_box notes that other schools may consider some of these acts differently (e.g., Shafi'is may view washing the private part as mustahabb but not necessarily sunnah). The Hanafi position is that these are sunnah muakkadah.
The thamarah (practical difference) is minimal: all schools agree these acts are recommended; the debate is about the precise category.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في سنن الغسل (١٧٠) و بشرة اللحية وبشرة الشارب والحاجب (١٧١) والفرج الخارج. فصل : (يسن في الاغتسال اثنا عشر شيئا. (١٧٢) الابتداء بالتسمية والنية وغسل اليدين الى الرسغين (١٧٣) وغسل نجاسة لو كانت وجه : (١) قالت عائشة كان رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم اذا اغتسل بدأ بيمينه فصب عليها من الماء فغسلها ثم صب الماء على الاذى الذي به بيمينه و غسل عنه بشماله حتى اذا فرغ من ذالک صب على رأسه. (٢) حدثتني خالتي ميمونة قالت : ادنيت لرسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم غسله من الجنابة فغسل كفيه مرتين او ثلاثا ثم ادخل يده في الاناء ثم افرغ به على فرجه و غسله بشماله ثم ضرب بشماله الارض فدلكها دلكاً شديدا ثم توضأ وضوئه للصلاة ثم افرغ على رأسه ثلاث حفنات ملء كفه ثم غسل سائر جسده ثم تنحى عن مقامه ذلك
Section on the sunnahs of ghusl: (170) And the skin of the beard, the skin of the mustache, and the eyebrow, (171) and the external private part. Section: Twelve things are sunnah in ghusl: (172) Beginning with the basmalah, intention, and washing the hands up to the wrists, (173) and washing impurity if present. Proof: (1) Aisha said: When the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) performed ghusl, he would begin with his right hand, pour water over it, wash it, then pour water over any impurity on his right hand and wash it off with his left, until when he finished that, he would pour water over his head. (2) My aunt Maimuna narrated: I placed water for the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) for ghusl from janabah, and he washed his hands twice or thrice, then put his hand into the vessel, then poured water over his private part and washed it with his left hand, then struck his left hand on the ground and rubbed it vigorously, then performed wudu like for prayer, then poured three handfuls of water over his head, then washed the rest of his body, then moved away from that place.
Source pages p. 140

Commentary
This passage is a section on the sunnahs of ghusl (ritual bath). It first clarifies a fard aspect: washing the skin beneath the beard, mustache, and eyebrows, as well as the external private part, is obligatory (fard) because water must reach those areas. Then it states that there are twelve sunnah acts in ghusl, listing the first few: beginning with basmalah and intention, washing hands to wrists, and washing any impurity on the body before ghusl. The author provides two hadith proofs from Aisha and Maimuna showing the Prophet's practice of washing his private part and removing impurity first. These actions are sunnah, not fard, but are recommended to follow the Prophet's example.

Key Terms
سنة (sunnah): A recommended act; doing it is rewarded, leaving it is not sinful but may be disliked (makruh tanzihi).
غسل (ghusl): Ritual bath performed after major impurity (janabah, menstruation, etc.).
فرج (farj): Private parts; external (farj kharij) must be washed in ghusl.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, how many sunnah acts are there in ghusl?
A) 10
B) 12
C) 8
D) 15

Key Takeaway
The sunnah acts of ghusl are derived from the Prophet's practice and are recommended but not obligatory; omission does not invalidate ghusl.

The Seven Sunnahs of Ghusl
Lists and explains the seven sunnahs of ghusl with proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the seven sunnah acts of ghusl according to the Hanafi school and state the proof for each.

Core Idea
The Prophet's practice establishes seven sunnahs for ghusl, including wudu before bathing and washing three times.

This passage from Thamaratun Najah outlines the seven recommended acts (sunnah) that the Prophet consistently performed during ghusl. Understanding these sunnahs helps you perfect your ritual bath with the same care as the Prophet. Each sunnah is supported by authentic hadith and analogy.

Guided Path
1
Identify the seven sunnahs from the matn
Read the numbered items in the matn (172-175) and list each sunnah. The first three are in (172), the next two in (173), the sixth in (174), and the seventh in (175).
2
Locate the evidence for each sunnah
For each sunnah, find the hadith or qiyas cited in the explanation. The hadith of Aisha and Maimuna provide evidence for most sunnahs; the hadith of Uthman and qiyas support the three-time washing.
3
Understand the rationale
Consider why each act is recommended: e.g., washing impurity separately prevents spreading; wudu before ghusl follows the Prophet's order; pouring three times mirrors wudu.
4
Distinguish sunnah from fard
Note that these acts are sunnah (recommended), not fard (obligatory). The proofs are from ahad hadith and qiyas, which in Hanafi usul indicate sunnah, not obligation.

ثمرة النجاح جلد اول
فصل في سنن الغسل
(۱۷۲ ) الابتداء بالتسمية والنية وغسل اليدين الى الرسغين (۱۷۳) وغسل نجاسة لو كانت بانفرادها وغسل فرجه (۱۷۴) ثم يتوضأ كوضوئه للصلوة فيثلث الغسل ويمسح الرأس ولكنه يؤخر غسل الرجلين ان كان يقف في محل يجتمع فيه الماء (۱۷۵) ثم يفيض الماء على بدنه ثلاثا ولو انغمس في الماء الجاري او ما في حكمه ومكث فقد اكمل السنة (١٦) ويبتدئ في صب الماء على رأسه ثم على منكبه الايمن ثم الايسر
ترجمه : (۱۷۲) غسل میں بارہ چیزیں سنت ہیں۔ [1] شروع میں بسم اللہ پڑھنا۔[۲] نیت کرنا۔[۳] دونوں ہاتھ دونوں پہونچوں تک دھونا۔
تشریح : غسل سے پہلے وضو کرنا سنت ہے، اور وضو میں بسم اللہ پڑھنا اور نیت کرنا سنت ہے اسی طرح دونوں ہاتھوں کو پہونچوں تک دھونا سنت ہے اس لئے غسل میں بھی یہ سنت ہیں۔ ان سنتوں کی دلیل فصل: بين في الوضوء ثمادية عشر هيا، مسئلہ نمبر ۸۴ سے مسئلہ نمبر ۱۰۰ تک میں دیکھیں۔
ترجمه : (۱۷۳) [۴] نجاست کا دھونا اگر بدن پر الگ سے لگی ہوئی ہو ۔ (۵) اپنی شرمگاہ دھونا۔
تشریح : اپنی شرمگاہ دھونا سنت ہے، اور اس کے علاوہ بدن کے کسی حصے پر نجاست لگی ہو تو غسل سے پہلے اس کو دھونا بھی سنت ہے، تا کہ یہ نجاست غسل کے درمیان جسم پر نہ پھیلے۔
وجه : (۱) قالت عائشة كان رسول الله علم اذا اغتسل بدأ بيمينه فصب عليها من الماء فغسلها ثم صب الماء على الاذى الذي به بيمينه و غسل عنه بشماله حتى اذا فرغ من ذالک صب على رأسه - (مسلم شریف، باب القدر المستحب من الماء في غسل الجنابة ، الخ ص ۱۴۴، نمبر ۷۲۹/۳۲۱) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ جہاں پر نجاست ہو اس کو بھی دھوتے تھے ۔ (۲) فرج دھونا مستقل سنت ہے اس کے لئے اور باقی سنتوں کے لئے یہ حدیث ہے۔ حدثتني خالتي ميمونة قالت : ادنيـت لـرسول الله الا الله غسله من الجنابة، فغسل كفيه مرتين او ثلاثا " ، ثم ادخل يده في الاناء ، ثم افرغ به علی فرجه ، و غسله بشماله ، ثم ضرب بشماله الارض ، فدلكها دلكاً شديدا، ثم توضأ وضوئه للصلاة ثم افرغ على رأسه ثلاث حفنات ملء كفه،ثم غسل سائر جسده ،ثم تنحى عن مقامه ذالک
فغسل رجليه ، ثم اتيته بالمنديل فرده ( مسلم شریف ، باب صفحه تغسل الجنابة، ص ۱۴۲، نمبر ۲۲/۳۱۷ ۷ ربخاری شریف ، باب الغسل مرة واحدة ، ص ۱۳۹، نمبر ۲۵۷ / ابو داود شریف ، باب فی الغسل من الجنابة ، ص ۴۵، نمبر ۲۴۵ر ترمذی شریف ، باب ماجاء فی الغسل من الجنابة ص ۲۸ نمبر ۱۰۳) اس حدیث سے ترتیب کے ساتھ سنتیں ثابت ہوئی ہیں۔
ترجمه : (۱۷۴) [۲] پھر نماز کے وضو کی طرح وضو کرنا، پس ہر ایک اعضاء کو تین تین مرتبہ دھوئے ، اور ایک مرتبہ سح کرے، اگر پانی جمع ہونے کی جگہ پر نسل کرتا ہو تو دونوں پاؤں غسل کے بعد دھوئے۔
تشریح : اوپر کی حدیث میں موجود ہے کہ حضور غسل سے پہلے نماز کی طرح وضو فرماتے ،اور یہ بھی ہے کہ پاؤں کے پاس پانی جمع تھا اس لئے وہاں سے ہٹنے کے بعد پاؤں دھویا تا کہ پاؤں دوبارہ نجس نہ ہو جائے۔
ترجمه : ( ۱۷۵ [۷] تمام بدن پر تین بار پانی بہانا۔ اور اگر جاری پانی میں ، یا جو جاری پانی کے حکم میں ہے غوطہ لگا کر ٹھہرا رہا تو سنت پوری ہو جائے گی۔
تشریح : وضو میں تین مرتبہ پانی بہانا سنت ہے اس لئے غسل میں بھی تین مرتبہ پانی بہانا سنت ہوگا۔ اور تالاب میں غوطہ لگایا ہوتو تھوڑی دیر غوطہ لگائے رکھنے سے تین مرتبہ کی سنت ادا ہو جائے گی۔
وجه : (1) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ ہر عضو کو تین تین مرتبہ دھوئے ، اور پورے سر پر مسح کرے۔ ان حمران مولی عثمان اخبره انه رأى عثمان بن عفان دعا باناء ، فافرغ على كفيه ثلاث مرار فغسلهما ، ثم ادخل يمينه في الاناء فمضمض واستنثر ثم غسل وجهه ثلاثا و يديه الى المرفقين ثلاث مرار ، ثم مسح برأسه ،ثم غسل رجليه ثلاث مرار الى الكعبين ، ثم قال : قال رسول الله الله : من توضأ نحو وضوئى هذا ثم صلى ركعتين لا يحدث فيهما نفسه غفر له ما تقدم من ذنبه - ( بخاری شریف ، باب الوضوء ثلاثا ثلا خا ص ۱۳۲، نمبر ۱۵۹ را بو داود شریف ، باب صفة وضور انبیصلى الله عليه وسلم ص ۲۶ نمبر ۱۰۸) بیحدیث وضو کے بارے میں ہے، اس پر قیاس کرتے ہوئے غسل میں بھی تین مرتبہ دھونا سنت ہے۔
خت : فیض : فاض سے مشتق ہے ، بہایا۔ انمس خمس سے مشتق ہے، غوطہ لگایا، ڈوبا۔ مکٹ بھہرارہا۔
Fruit of Success Volume 1
Chapter on the Sunnahs of Ghusl
(172) Beginning with saying Bismillah, intention, and washing the hands up to the wrists. (173) And washing impurity if it is separately on the body, and washing his private part. (174) Then he performs wudu like his wudu for prayer, so he washes each limb three times and wipes the head, but he delays washing the feet if he is standing in a place where water collects. (175) Then he pours water over his body three times, and if he dives into flowing water or what is in its ruling and stays, he has completed the sunnah. And he begins pouring water on his head, then on his right shoulder, then on his left.
Translation: (172) Twelve things are sunnah in ghusl. [1] Reciting Bismillah at the start. [2] Making intention. [3] Washing both hands up to the wrists.
Explanation: It is sunnah to perform wudu before ghusl, and in wudu, reciting Bismillah and making intention are sunnah, likewise washing both hands up to the wrists is sunnah. Therefore, these are also sunnah in ghusl. The proof for these sunnahs: see the chapter on wudu, from issue 84 to issue 100.
Translation: (173) [4] Washing impurity if it is separately on the body. (5) Washing his private part.
Explanation: Washing his private part is sunnah, and if there is impurity on any part of the body besides that, washing it before ghusl is also sunnah, so that this impurity does not spread on the body during the ghusl.
Proof: (1) Aisha said: The Messenger of Allah, when he performed ghusl, would begin with his right hand and pour water on it and wash it, then pour water on the impurity that was on it with his right hand and wash it off with his left hand until when he finished that, he poured water on his head - (Muslim, Chapter on the Desirable Amount of Water in Ghusl from Janabah, etc., p. 144, no. 729/321). In this hadith, he used to wash the place where there was impurity. (2) Washing the private part is an independent sunnah, and for it and the other sunnahs, this hadith: My maternal aunt Maimuna narrated: I brought water for the Messenger of Allah for ghusl from janabah. He washed his hands twice or three times, then put his hand into the vessel, then poured water on his private part and washed it with his left hand, then struck his left hand on the ground and rubbed it vigorously, then performed wudu like his wudu for prayer, then poured three handfuls of water on his head, then washed the rest of his body, then moved from that place and washed his feet. Then I brought him a towel and he returned it. (Muslim, Chapter on Ghusl from Janabah, p. 142, no. 22/317; Bukhari, Chapter on Ghusl Once, p. 139, no. 257; Abu Dawud, Chapter on Ghusl from Janabah, p. 45, no. 245; Tirmidhi, Chapter on Ghusl from Janabah, p. 28, no. 103). From this hadith, the sunnahs are established in order.
Translation: (174) [6] Then perform wudu like his wudu for prayer, so wash each limb three times and wipe the head once, and if he is standing in a place where water collects, he should wash both feet after the ghusl.
Explanation: In the above hadith, the Prophet performed wudu like for prayer before ghusl, and it also mentions that water collected near his feet, so he washed his feet after moving away so that the feet would not become impure again.
Translation: (175) [7] Pouring water over the entire body three times. And if he dives into flowing water, or what is in the ruling of flowing water, and stays, the sunnah is fulfilled.
Explanation: Pouring water three times is sunnah in wudu, so it is also sunnah in ghusl. And if he dives into a pond, staying submerged for a short time fulfills the sunnah of three times.
Proof: (1) In this hadith, he washed each limb three times and wiped the entire head. Humran, the freed slave of Uthman, informed him that he saw Uthman bin Affan call for a vessel, poured water on his hands three times and washed them, then put his right hand into the vessel, rinsed his mouth and nose, then washed his face three times, and his hands up to the elbows three times, then wiped his head, then washed his feet three times up to the ankles, then said: The Messenger of Allah said: Whoever performs wudu like my wudu and then prays two rak'ahs without talking to himself, his previous sins are forgiven. (Bukhari, Chapter on Wudu Three Times, p. 132, no. 159; Abu Dawud, Chapter on the Description of the Wudu of the Prophet, p. 26, no. 108). This hadith is about wudu, and by analogy (qiyas), washing three times in ghusl is also sunnah.
Vocabulary: Fayd: derived from fada, meaning poured. Inghamasa: derived from khamasa, meaning dived. Makatha: remained.
Source pages p. 141

Commentary
This passage from Thamaratun Najah explains the seven sunnahs (recommended acts) of ghusl (ritual bath). The author first presents the matn (text) listing the sunnahs, then provides an Urdu translation and commentary (tashrih), followed by proofs (wajh) from hadith. The passage is a typical expansion probe where the commentator clarifies each sunnah and its evidence.

The first three sunnahs (172) are beginning with Bismillah, making intention, and washing the hands up to the wrists. These are sunnah in wudu as well, so they carry over to ghusl. The proof is referenced to earlier chapters.

The next two sunnahs (173) are washing any impurity on the body separately and washing the private parts. The purpose is to remove impurity before the main wash to prevent spreading. Proof is given from the hadith of Aisha and the hadith of Maimuna, showing the Prophet's practice.

The sixth sunnah (174) is performing wudu before ghusl, washing each limb three times and wiping the head once, but delaying washing the feet if standing in a place where water collects. This is from the Maimuna hadith where the Prophet moved to wash his feet to avoid impure water.

The seventh sunnah (175) is pouring water over the entire body three times, or diving into flowing water and staying submerged. This is derived by analogy (qiyas) from wudu, where washing limbs three times is sunnah. The proof is from the hadith of Uthman describing the Prophet's wudu, and the commentator applies qiyas to ghusl.

The Hanafi position is that these acts are sunnah (recommended), not obligatory (fard). The proofs are sound hadiths from Sahih collections.

Key Terms
غسل (ghusl): The ritual bath to remove major impurity (janabah, menstruation, etc.)
سنة (sunnah): Recommended act in ghusl; omission does not invalidate ghusl, but following it is meritorious
وضوء (wudu): Ablution performed before ghusl as a sunnah act

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on washing impurity from the body before performing ghusl?
A) It is fard (obligatory).
B) It is sunnah (recommended) to prevent spreading impurity.
C) It is makruh (disliked) if the impurity is dry.
D) It is only required if the impurity is najis 'ayn.

Key Takeaway
The seven sunnahs of ghusl are based on the Prophet's practice and are recommended but not obligatory; following them perfects the ritual bath.

Washing Private Part and Wudu Before Ghusl
First sunnah of ghusl: washing impurity and performing wudu

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two sunnah acts of ghusl (washing private part and wudu), explain why wudu before ghusl is sunnah not fard, and apply the condition for delaying foot washing.

Core Idea
Wudu before ghusl is sunnah, not fard — its proof is the Prophet's practice, and its form mirrors prayer wudu.

This passage opens the discussion on the sunnan (recommended acts) of ghusl. It explains that the first sunnah is to wash any impurity on the private part separately, then perform wudu exactly as for prayer, with a specific exception: if one is standing where water collects, foot washing is delayed until after the ghusl. The proof is a hadith from Uthman describing the Prophet's wudu, applied by qiyas to ghusl. Understanding this clarifies the distinction between obligatory (fard) and recommended (sunnah) acts in purification.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What exactly is being ruled upon? It is the first sunnah of ghusl: washing the private part separately and performing wudu. The ruling level is sunnah muakkadah.
The passage uses the term 'sunnah' explicitly.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is the hadith of Uthman (narrated by Humran) describing the Prophet's wudu. This is a hadith ahad with zanni thubut, cited to establish the recommended form.
The hadith is quoted in full in the source.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does this hadith prove the sunnah of wudu in ghusl? The Prophet's action shows how wudu should be done, and he commanded it for prayer; applying it to ghusl by analogy (qiyas) makes it sunnah, not fard, because the command is not explicitly for ghusl.
Hanafi usul classifies the imperative as indicating wujub, but here the context and other evidence lower it to sunnah.
4
Note the condition and exception
The wudu is performed as for prayer, but if the person is standing where water collects (like a shower tray), he delays washing his feet until after the ghusl to avoid re‑soiling them with impurity.
This conditional exception is a practical point in the Hanafi school.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The Hanafi school relies on this as the muftā bihi position. The wudu before ghusl is sunnah, not fard. There is no significant intra‑Hanafi disagreement.
The authority weight is zahir al‑riwayah from the core books.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في سنن الغسل بانفرادها وغسل فرجه (١٧٤) ثم يتوضأ كوضوئه للصلوة فيثلث الغسل ويمسح الرأس ولكنه يؤخر غسل الرجلين ان كان يقف في محل يجتمع فيه الماء. ان حمران مولي عثمان اخبره انه رأى عثمان بن عفان دعا باناء ، فافرغ على كفيه ثلاث مرار فغسلهما ، ثم ادخل يمينه في الاناء فمضمض واستنثر ثم غسل وجهه ثلاثا و يديه الى المرفقين ثلاث مرار ، ثم مسح برأسه ،ثم غسل رجليه ثلاث مرار الى الكعبين ، ثم قال : قال رسول الله الله : من توضأ نحو وضوئى هذا ثم صلى ركعتين لا يحدث فيهما نفسه غفر له ما تقدم من ذنبه
Chapter on the Sunnahs of Ghusl: Washing it separately and washing his private part. Then he performs wudu like his wudu for prayer, washing each limb three times and wiping his head, but he delays washing his feet if he is standing in a place where water collects. Humran, the freed slave of Uthman, informed him that he saw Uthman ibn Affan call for a vessel and pour water over his hands three times, washing them; then he put his right hand into the vessel, rinsed his mouth and nose, then washed his face three times and his forearms three times, then wiped his head, then washed his feet three times up to the ankles. Then he said: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'Whoever performs wudu like this wudu of mine, then prays two rak'ahs without letting anything distract him, his previous sins will be forgiven.'

Commentary
This is a ruling_with_proof passage presenting the first sunnah of ghusl: washing any impurity on the private part separately, then performing wudu exactly as for prayer. The wudu includes washing each limb three times and wiping the head once. However, if the person is standing on a surface where water collects (making the feet vulnerable to impurity), he delays washing his feet until after the ghusl. The proof is the hadith of Uthman describing the Prophet's wudu, which is applied to ghusl by analogy (qiyas). The Hanafi school holds that this wudu is sunnah, not fard, in ghusl.

Key Terms
بانفرادها (bānfirādihā): Washing the private part separately from the rest of the body if there is impurity on it.
سنة الغسل (sunnat al-ghusl): Acts recommended by the Prophet during ghusl; omission does not invalidate ghusl but loses reward.

Key Takeaway
The first sunnah of ghusl is to wash the private part separately, then perform wudu as for prayer, with the option to delay foot washing if water collects.

The Second Sunnah of Ghusl: Three Pours or Immersion
Second sunnah of ghusl: pouring water three times or immersion

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the second sunnah of ghusl and explain how immersion in flowing water fulfills it.

Core Idea
Pouring water three times in ghusl is sunnah; immersion in flowing water suffices.

After the first sunnah steps of washing hands and private parts, the main sunnah of ghusl is to pour water over the entire body three times. The Prophet (ﷺ) practiced this regularly. The Hanafi school adds that if one immerses in flowing water (like a river) and stays submerged briefly, the sunnah is achieved without separate pours. This flexibility shows the school's practical accommodation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage describes the second sunnah of ghusl: pouring water three times. The ruling is sunnah muakkadah.
Sunnah muakkadah means confirmed and recommended, not obligatory.
2
Understand the two methods
Two options are given: 1) pour water three times; 2) immerse in flowing water and remain for a while. Both achieve the sunnah.
Immersion must be in flowing water or its equivalent (e.g., a large tank with circulation).
3
Recognize the Hanafi proof
The proof is the Prophet's practice of three pours. The alternative of immersion is derived from qiyas (analogy) with three washes in wudu
The hadith is not quoted but is well-known in fiqh.
4
Note cross-madhhab difference
Some schools do not specify three times; they consider covering the whole body once as mustahabb, not a confirmed sunnah.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم يفيض الماء على بدنه ثلاثا ولو انغمس في الماء الجارى او ما في حكمه ومكث فقد اكمل السنة
Then he pours water over his body three times, and if he immerses himself in flowing water or what is considered like it and remains [for a while], then he has completed the sunnah.
Source pages p. 142

Commentary
This is a ruling_with_proof passage stating the second sunnah of ghusl: after the initial wudu, the person pours water over the entire body three times. Alternatively, if one immerses completely in flowing water (such as a river) or a body of water that is considered like flowing (e.g., a large tank with circulation) and stays submerged for a short duration, the sunnah of three pours is considered fulfilled. The proof is based on the general practice of the Prophet, who used to pour water three times over his body. The Hanafi school derives this from hadith and qiyas (analogy) with the three-time washing in wudu.

Key Terms
فيض (fayad): Pouring or flowing water over the body.
انغمس (inghamasa): To immerse or submerge oneself completely in water.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Pouring water twice and then immersing.
B) Immersion in flowing water with a short stay.
C) Pouring water five times.
D) Immersion in any water, flowing or not.

Key Takeaway
The confirmed sunnah is three pours or one immersion in flowing water.

Sunnah Order of Washing Head and Shoulders in Ghusl
Third sunnah: order of washing head, right, then left shoulder

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the sunnah order of washing in ghusl and explain the hadith evidence for this order.

Core Idea
The sunnah order: head, then right shoulder, then left shoulder.

In ghusl, certain actions are sunnah mu'akkadah, adding completeness to the purification. One such sunnah is the order of washing the upper body. This lesson presents the recommended sequence of pouring water over the head and shoulders, supported by a hadith from Aisha (may Allah be pleased with her).

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What specific act is being described? What is the legal classification of this act (fard, wajib, sunnah, etc.)?
The act is the order of washing in ghusl. The ruling is sunnah mu'akkadah.
2
Locate the dalil (proof)
Find the hadith quoted in the passage. Identify its source and type (e.g., ahad hadith).
The hadith is from Sunan Abu Dawud, describing the Prophet's ghusl.
3
Analyse the wajh al-dalalah (how the proof indicates the ruling)
How exactly does this hadith prove the recommended order? Is it a command or an action?
The Prophet's action (starting with the right side, then left) is taken as an indication of sunnah.
4
Consider the hukm level and its implications
Why is this considered sunnah and not wajib? What is the consequence of neglecting the order?
The proof is a single narration (ahad) and describes an action without an explicit command, so it establishes sunnah, not obligation.
5
Note cross-madhhab differences
Do other schools agree on this order and its emphasis?
Some schools consider it mustahabb but not as strongly emphasized as sunnah mu'akkadah.

Rubbing the Body and Continuity in Ghusl
Fourth sunnah: rubbing body and doing ghusl consecutively

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the sunnah ruling for rubbing (dalk) and continuity (muwalat) in ghusl and explain the evidence from the hadith of Aisha.

Core Idea
Rubbing ensures water reaches every part; continuity maintains the sunnah sequence — omission does not invalidate ghusl.

This lesson covers two recommended practices during ghusl: rubbing the body (dalk) and performing the acts without lengthy interruption (muwalat). The Hanafi school considers these as sunnah mu'akkadah, based on the prophetic practice reported by Aisha. Understanding their status helps distinguish between what is obligatory and what is meritorious in purification.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Recognize that both dalk and muwalat are being ruled as sunnah. Note that they are not fard or wajib.
The author explicitly states these as practices to be followed.
2
Locate the dalil
Find the hadith of Aisha about Asma asking regarding ghusl from menstruation. This is the proof.
The hadith is ahad but considered reliable.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The phrase 'rubs it vigorously until the water reaches the roots of her hair' indicates that rubbing is recommended to ensure complete coverage.
By qiyas, this applies to all ghusl, not just menstrual.
4
Note the ikhtilaf and mufta bihi
Other schools also recommend rubbing but may not emphasize continuity as a separate sunnah. The Hanafi mufta bihi is that both are sunnah mu'akkadah.
Consult the al-mukhtalaf fih section for details.

The proof is the hadith of Aisha regarding ghusl from menstruation: the woman pours water over her head and rubs it vigorously. This hadith shows rubbing is recommended. The Hanafi school considers both rubbing and continuity as sunnah.

Etiquettes of Ghusl: Mirroring Wudu with One Exception
Etiquettes of ghusl: same as wudu except facing qibla

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the etiquettes of ghusl and identify the exception regarding facing the qibla, explaining why it is disliked.

Core Idea
The adab of ghusl mirror wudu except facing the qibla—exposure of awrah makes it disliked.

This lesson focuses on the recommended practices (adab) for ghusl. The Hanafi school teaches that these are essentially the same as those for wudu, with one key exception: facing the qibla during ghusl is disliked (makruh) because the private parts are typically uncovered. Understanding this distinction helps maintain respect for the qibla while fulfilling the obligation of ghusl.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the act and its category
Identify that ghusl is a purification ritual (ibadah) with obligatory (fard) and recommended (adab) components. The passage specifically addresses the adab.
Adab are sunnan (recommended acts) that enhance the worship.
2
Compare with wudu adab
The passage states that the adab of ghusl are identical to those of wudu. Recall that wudu adab include starting with the right side, using the right hand, washing each part in order, etc.
You may need to reference a separate lesson on wudu adab for the full list.
3
Identify the exception
The only difference is facing the qibla. In wudu, facing qibla is recommended; in ghusl, it is disliked (makruh tanzih).
The reason provided: ghusl often involves uncovering the awrah.
4
Understand the ruling on facing qibla
Facing the qibla with exposed awrah is considered disrespectful. Therefore, it is mildly disliked. If the awrah is covered completely, it is not disliked.
The ruling is makruh tanzihi, not haram.
5
Note the carryover of other disliked acts
All other disliked acts in wudu (e.g., extravagance in water, spitting in the water source) are equally disliked in ghusl.
This is based on the principle: 'what is disliked in wudu is disliked in ghusl'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل : (١٧٨) و آداب الاغتسال هي آداب الوضوء الا انه لا يستقبل القبلة لانه يكون غالبا مع كشف العورة وكُره فيه ما كُره في الوضوء.
Chapter: (178) The etiquettes of ghusl are the etiquettes of wudu, except that one does not face the qibla because ghusl is often with uncovering the private parts, and what is disliked in wudu is disliked in ghusl.
Source pages p. 143

Commentary
This is a ruling_statement passage presenting the etiquettes (adab) of ghusl. They are identical to those of wudu, which include starting with the right side, using the right hand for cleaning, not facing the qibla when relieving oneself, etc. However, in ghusl, facing the qibla is disliked (makruh) because the person is often naked or partially covered (awrah exposed). Therefore, it is recommended to avoid facing the qibla during ghusl. All other disliked acts in wudu (e.g., extravagance in water, spitting in the water source) are similarly disliked in ghusl. The Hanafi school bases this on general principles of respect for the qibla and modesty.

Key Terms
آداب الغسل (ādāb al-ghusl): Recommended practices in ghusl, derived from the sunnah.
استقبال القبلة (istiqbāl al-qiblah): Facing the direction of the Kaaba during an act.

D) There is no such dislike.

Key Takeaway
The adab of ghusl are identical to wudu except that facing the qibla is disliked due to awrah exposure; other disliked acts carry over.

Sunnah Acts and Etiquettes of Ghusl
Rulings with hadith proofs on sunan and adab of ghusl

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the sunnah acts of ghusl and explain the exception regarding facing qiblah in its etiquettes.

Core Idea
Sunnah acts enhance ghusl; adab mirror wudu but avoid qiblah due to 'awrah exposure.

Ghusl (ritual bath) has mandatory acts (fardh) and recommended acts (sunnah) that perfect the purification. This passage presents the sunnah practices derived from the Prophet's example and explains that the etiquettes of ghusl follow those of wudu, with a key exception: facing qiblah is disliked because the private parts are typically uncovered. Understanding these sunan helps you perform ghusl in a complete and rewarding manner.

Guided Path
1
Identify the sunnah acts
Scan the first part of the passage to list the four sunnah acts mentioned: pouring water over the head first, washing the right shoulder, then the left, rubbing the body, and performing the washing consecutively.
These are based on the Prophet's practice (fi'l).
2
Understand the etiquettes (adab) rule
The passage states that the adab of ghusl are the same as those of wudu—except for facing qiblah. Recall the wudu adab (e.g., using the right hand, rinsing mouth, etc.) and note the general principle that ghusl shares rulings with wudu unless specified otherwise.
Adab are mustahabb; omitting them is not sinful.
3
Note the exception regarding qiblah
Facing qiblah is disliked in ghusl because the 'awrah is usually exposed. This overrides the sunnah of facing qiblah from wudu adab. Understand that the ruling is linked to the condition of 'awrah exposure.
If one can cover the 'awrah, the dislikedness may be removed; the text says 'usually'.
4
Recognize the evidence (dalil)
The passage cites two hadith: Aisha describing the Prophet's ghusl (sequence and rubbing) and her narration about Asma's question on menstrual bath (pouring and rubbing hair). These actions are the basis for the sunnah acts.
The hadith are ahad (single-transmitter) but sufficient for establishing sunnah.

مكروه (makruh): Disliked act; avoiding it is rewarded but doing it is not sinful.

Occasions for Which Ghusl is Sunnah
Lists four occasions for sunnah ghusl with hadith proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the four occasions for sunnah ghusl and explain the Hanafi interpretation of the hadith proofs.

Core Idea
Friday and Eid ghusl are sunnah muakkadah, not wajib, per Hanafi interpretation.

This passage lists the four occasions when performing ghusl is a strongly recommended sunnah. It provides two hadith proofs that students often misinterpret as indicating obligation. Understanding the Hanafi method of weighing proofs is key to arriving at the correct ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is ghusl on these four occasions. The ruling is sunnah muakkadah (emphasized recommended).
Not wajib or fard.
2
Locate the dalil
Two hadith: from Abu Sa'id al-Khudri about Friday, and from Ibn Abbas about Eid.
Both are ahad hadith, so zanni al-thubut.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The first hadith uses 'wajib' but Hanafi interprets it as emphatic recommendation based on usul principles. The second shows the Prophet's continuous practice (fi'l), indicating sunnah.
Fi'l alone does not confer wujub in Hanafi usul.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Some schools (e.g., Hanbali) consider Friday ghusl wajib. Hanafi says sunnah muakkadah.
A legitimate difference of ijtihad.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The mufta bihi is sunnah muakkadah; omitting it is not sinful but leaves a recommended act.
Consistency with Hanafi principles of interpreting commands.

Four Occasions for Sunnah Ghusl: Friday, Eid, Ihram, Arafah
Ruling with proof listing four sunnah ghusl occasions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the four occasions for which ghusl is sunnah, state the Hanafi ruling of sunnah muakkadah for each, and explain why the word 'wajib' in the Friday hadith indicates emphasis rather than legal obligation.

Core Idea
Ghusl for Friday, Eid, ihram, and Arafah is emphatically recommended but not obligatory — the command is one of encouragement, not compulsion.

This passage from Thamarat al-Najah identifies four specific occasions when performing a full bath (ghusl) is considered a strongly recommended act (sunnah muakkadah) in the Hanafi school. Each occasion — Friday prayer, Eid prayer, entering ihram, and standing at Arafah — involves communal gatherings, and the Prophet ﷺ emphasised cleanliness for them. While some hadiths use strong language like 'wajib', Hanafi scholars interpret this as ta'kid (emphasis) rather than legal obligation, distinguishing the school from positions that consider it obligatory.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four occasions
Read the text and list the four specific times when ghusl is recommended: Friday prayer, the two Eid prayers, entering ihram, and for the pilgrim at Arafah after noon (zawal).
These are distinct from obligatory ghusl for janabah, hayd, and nifas.
2
Understand the Hanafi ruling
Recognise that the ruling for each occasion is sunnah muakkadah (emphasised sunnah) — not fard, not wajib. The act carries reward but omission does not invalidate the prayer or ritual.
The word 'sunnah' here means recommended, not the technical sunnah category in Usul.
3
Analyse the proof for each occasion
For each occasion, identify the specific hadith or practice cited. Friday: hadith of Abu Sa'id al-Khudri using 'wajib'. Eid: practice of the Prophet. Arafah: practice and statement of Ibrahim al-Nakha'i. Ihram: hadith of Zayd ibn Thabit.
All proofs are ahad and zanni al-thubut.
4
Examine the key debate: the word 'wajib'
The Friday hadith says 'wajib' — Hanafis interpret this as ta'kid (emphasis) because the threshold for obligation (fard/wajib) requires definitive evidence. The hadith is ahad, so it cannot impose a legal obligation. The Prophet’s consistent practice without rebuking those who omitted it supports this.
This is the core dispute with the Shafii school, which regards it as wajib.
5
Compare with the Shafii position
Know that Imam al-Shafii considers Friday ghusl wajib (obligatory) based on the same hadith, taking 'wajib' literally. The practical difference: Hanafis do not require ghusl for a valid Friday prayer; Shafiis consider it necessary (though the prayer still valid if omitted without excuse).
Thamarah al-khilaf: whether the prayer is considered deficient if ghusl is omitted.

محتلم (muhtalim): One who has reached puberty (literally: one who has had a wet dream). The hadith addresses all adults.

Ghusl as Mandub for Sixteen Occasions
Lists occasions for mandub ghusl

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling level (mandub) for each listed occasion and distinguish mandub from sunnah muakkadah in Hanafi fiqh.

Core Idea
Ghusl is mandub, not sunnah, for these sixteen occasions — a desirable act that earns reward but not extra emphasis.

The source lists sixteen occasions when performing ghusl is recommended (mandub). While often called 'sunnah ghusl' in common speech, the Hanafi school classifies them as mandub/mustahabb — a category below sunnah muakkadah. Understanding this distinction prevents conflating levels of recommendation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling level
The act is ghusl (full body wash). The ruling level stated in the source is 'mandub' (or 'mustahabb'), meaning it is recommended but not strongly emphasized.
Do not confuse with sunnah muakkadah, which is more strongly emphasized.
2
List the legible occasions from the text
Extract the occasions that are readable despite OCR corruption: 1) when an unbeliever becomes Muslim, 2) when a child reaches puberty, 3) when a mad person regains sanity, 4) after cupping, 5) after washing a deceased, 6) on Shab-e-Barat, 7) on Laylat al-Qadr, 8) for entering Madinah, 9) for staying at Muzdalifah on Yawm al-Nahr, 10) for entering Makkah, 11) for Tawaf al-Ziyarah.
The exact sixteen are not fully recoverable; this is a partial list.
3
Analyze the ruling level: mandub vs. sunnah
Mandub (mustahabb) means performing the act yields reward, omitting it incurs no sin. It is less emphasized than sunnah muakkadah, which is a confirmed practice of the Prophet (ﷺ).
In Hanafi fiqh, mandub is a distinct category; some later scholars equate it with sunnah ghayr muakkadah.
4
Apply the ruling to a new scenario
If a person asks: 'Is ghusl obligatory for entering Makkah?' the answer is no; it is mandub. This distinction matters in knowing what is required vs. recommended.
The evidence for mandub is weaker than for sunnah muakkadah, often based on general encouragement rather than specific emphasis.

لیلۃ القدر میں، جب معلوم ہو، مدینہ طیبہ میں داخل ہونے کے لئے۔ یوم نحر کی صبح کو مزدلفہ میں ٹھہرنے کے لئے ۔
مکہ معظمہ میں داخل ہونے کے لئے ۔
ال... طواف زیارت کے لئے ۔
Ghusl is recommended in sixteen things. Chapter on what ghusl is desirable for: 16. Ghusl is mustahabb for: [...] a pure person who becomes Muslim, [...] who has reached puberty, [...] who recovers from insanity, after cupping, after washing a deceased, on Shab-e-Barat, on Laylat al-Qadr when known, for entering Madinah, for staying at Muzdalifah on the morning of Yawm al-Nahr, for entering Makkah, for Tawaf al-Ziyarah.
Source pages p. 145

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement listing sixteen occasions for which ghusl is desirable (mandub or mustahabb). The author does not provide proofs here; it is a memorization anchor. The list includes: (1) when an unbeliever becomes Muslim, (2) when a child reaches puberty, (3) when a mad person regains sanity, (4) after cupping (hijama), (5) after washing a deceased, (6) on the night of mid-Sha'ban (Shab-e-Barat), (7) on Laylat al-Qadr if known, (8) for entering Madinah, (9) on the morning of the 10th of Dhul-Hijjah at Muzdalifah, (10) for entering Makkah, (11) for Tawaf al-Ziyarah, and others not fully legible. The term 'mandub' is used interchangeably with 'mustahabb', meaning a recommended act that yields reward but no punishment for leaving. It is a lower rank than sunnah.

Key Terms
مندوب (mandub): A recommended action that is desirable but not as strongly emphasized as sunnah. Doing it earns reward, leaving it does not incur sin.
مستحب (mustahabb): Same as mandub, a desirable act.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on ghusl after cupping according to the passage?
A) Wajib
B) Sunnah muakkadah
C) Mandub (mustahabb)
D) Fard

Key Takeaway
Ghusl for these sixteen occasions is mandub (mustahabb), not sunnah muakkadah or wajib.

Taharah — Purification
intermediate

Sixteen Occasions for Recommended Ghusl (Mustahabb)
Lists sixteen actions for which ghusl is mustahabb with proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the sixteen occasions for which ghusl is mustahabb in the Hanafi school and identify the proofs for the first six items.

Core Idea
Ghusl on sixteen occasions is mustahabb, not obligatory—rewarded if done, not sinful if left.

This passage from Thamaratun Najah explains the occasions on which ghusl (full body wash) is recommended (mustahabb). The author lists sixteen items, some supported by hadith and some by the practice of the Companions. The lesson focuses on the first few items and the distinction between mustahabb and obligatory ghusl.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act is ghusl on specific occasions. The author states the ruling is mustahabb (recommended), which in Hanafi fiqh is equivalent to sunnah ghayr muakkadah.
Mustahabb means performing it is rewarded but omitting it is not sinful.
2
Examine the proofs for key occasions
The author provides hadith for ghusl on Eid, Arafah, and ihram, and athar for other occasions. For embracing Islam while pure, the hadith of Thumamah is cited. For recovery from insanity, the hadith of Aisha about the Prophet's illness is used.
The proofs are all from authentic sources.
3
Understand the hukm level
The text emphasizes that ghusl on these occasions is not obligatory. For example, a person who becomes Muslim while pure does not need to perform ghusl for janabah; it is only recommended.
This contrasts with ghusl for janabah, which is obligatory.
4
Classify each occasion
Go through the sixteen occasions and categorize them: those with direct hadith (Eid, Arafah, ihram), those with athar (post-midday on Arafah), those implied by practice (cupping, washing the deceased), and those without specific proof (night of Bara'ah, etc.) as the author notes.
Some occasions are derived from general principles rather than explicit texts.
5
Apply to modern scenarios
Consider a new Muslim who never experienced janabah: no obligation to perform ghusl, but it is recommended. Similarly, a person who turns 15 without nocturnal emission may perform ghusl as a recommended act.
The ruling is relaxed: it is better to do it, but not required.

Thamaratun Najah volume 1, page 144. Ghusl is recommended in sixteen things. Section: What is recommended for ghusl. Proof: (1) From his grandfather al-Fakah ibn Sa'd, who was a Companion: the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) used to perform ghusl on the day of Fitr, day of Nahr, and day of Arafah, and al-Fakah used to order his family to perform ghusl on these days. (Ibn Majah, chapter on ghusl on the two Eids, p. 186, no. 1316). In this hadith is that on Arafah, i.e., the 9th of Dhul Hijjah, he performed ghusl. (2) And for ghusl after midday, there is this athar: From Ibrahim: he said: proceed to Arafat, and when midday comes, perform ghusl if you find water, otherwise perform wudu. (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, chapter on what is mentioned about ghusl on the day of Arafah in Hajj, vol. 3, p. 404, no. 15558). In this saying of a Tabi'i is that ghusl after midday on the day of Arafah is mustahabb. (3) For ihram, he performed ghusl. Its proof is this hadith: From Kharijah ibn Zayd ibn Thabit from his father: that he saw the Prophet (peace be upon him) strip for his talbiyah and perform ghusl. (Tirmidhi, chapter on ghusl at ihram, p. 71, no. 830; Muslim, chapter on validity of ihram of a menstruating woman and recommendation of ghusl for ihram, p. 385, no. 2908/1209). From this hadith it is known that ghusl for ihram is sunnah. For sixteen things ghusl is mustahabb: one who is pure and becomes Muslim, one who reaches puberty by age, one who recovers from insanity, after cupping, after washing a deceased person, on the night of Bara'ah, on Laylat al-Qadr when known, for entering Madinah Tayyibah, for staying at Muzdalifah on the morning of the Day of Nahr, for entering Makkah al-Muazzamah, for... for Tawaf al-Ziyarah. [Page 146] Thamaratun Najah volume 1, page 145. Section: What is recommended for ghusl. (180) For one who becomes Muslim while pure. (181) For one who reaches puberty by age and for one who recovers from insanity. (182) And at cupping, and 12. For the prayer of solar eclipse or lunar eclipse, for Salat al-Istisqa, about 10, for something fearful... darkness of day, for a strong wind. Important note: Some acts below are important, and some are acts of worship; therefore ghusl for them is not sunnah but mustahabb. If one does it, it is good, and if not, there is no harm. Therefore for many acts, no hadith or saying of a Companion is found for performing ghusl. Translation: (180) Ghusl is mustahabb in sixteen things. [1] One who becomes Muslim while pure. Explanation: If a disbeliever becomes Muslim in a state of janabah, then performing ghusl to remove janabah is obligatory upon him. But if he becomes Muslim while pure, ghusl is not obligatory upon him, rather it is mustahabb. Proof: He heard Abu Hurairah... He said: Release Thumamah; then he went to a palm grove near the mosque, performed ghusl, then entered the mosque and said: I bear witness that there is no god but Allah and that Muhammad is the Messenger of Allah. (Bukhari, chapter on ghusl when one becomes Muslim and tying the prisoner in the mosque, p. 80, no. 462). In this hadith is that he performed ghusl for embracing Islam. Translation: (181) [2] One who reaches puberty by age. [3] One who recovers from insanity. Explanation: One who reaches puberty by emission of semen or by intercourse, then ghusl for janabah is obligatory upon him. But one whose semen has not come out and has reached the age of fifteen, by which he is considered an adult, then it is mustahabb for him to perform ghusl. No hadith found. [For] one who experienced insanity and then regains consciousness, it is better to perform ghusl. Proof: He said: I entered upon Aisha and said: Will you not tell me about the illness of the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him)? ... She said: So we did, and he performed ghusl, then he went to get up but fainted, then regained consciousness and said: Have the people prayed? We said: No, they are waiting for you, O Messenger of Allah. He said: Put water in the vessel for me. She said: He sat and performed ghusl, then went to get up but fainted, then regained consciousness, and said: Have the people prayed? We said: No, they are waiting for you, O Messenger of Allah. He said: Put water in the vessel for me. He sat and performed ghusl, then...
Source pages p. 145

Commentary
This passage is a ruling-with-proof on the topic of recommended ghusl (mustahabb). The author begins by stating that ghusl is recommended in sixteen things, then devotes a section to explaining each with proofs. The first three items are supported by hadith: ghusl on Eid al-Fitr, Eid al-Adha, and the day of Arafah (from al-Fakah ibn Sa'd); ghusl after midday on Arafah (from Ibrahim al-Nakha'i); and ghusl for ihram (from Zayd ibn Thabit). Then a list of sixteen items is given, with numbers missing in the OCR. The text continues on page 146 with specific numbering: (180) for one who becomes Muslim while pure, (181) for one who reaches puberty by age and for one who recovers from insanity, and (182) at cupping, plus other items like solar/lunar eclipse prayer, istisqa, etc. The author adds an important note that these are not sunnah but mustahabb. Then a detailed explanation for the first three items: for a pure person embracing Islam, ghusl is not obligatory but mustahabb (proof from hadith of Thumamah); for puberty by age (without emission), ghusl is mustahabb (no hadith); for recovering from insanity, it is better (proof from hadith of Aisha about the Prophet's illness). The Hanafi position is that mustahabb is a recommended act; omitting it is not sinful. The proofs are all from authentic hadith or athar.

Key Terms
مستحب (mustahabb): An act recommended but not obligatory; performing it is rewarded, omitting it is not sinful.
غسل (ghusl): The ritual washing of the entire body with water.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Fard
B) Wajib
C) Mustahabb
D) Sunnah muakkadah

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, ghusl is mustahabb on sixteen occasions, proven by hadith and athar; it is not obligatory but recommended.

Taharah — Purification
beginner
6 min
Recommended Ghusl (Mustahabb Bath) on Various Occasions
Lists occasions for recommended ghusl with hadith proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the occasions for which ghusl is mustahabb according to the Hanafi school, and identify the hadith evidence for each.

Core Idea
Ghusl is recommended for many occasions: purification, sacred places, and natural events — each proven by hadith or analogy.

This passage from Thamaratun Najah enumerates the occasions when performing a full body wash (ghusl) is recommended. These include acts related to hajj, after washing the deceased, after cupping, on special nights, and during extraordinary events like eclipses. The author provides hadith proofs for most and uses qiyas for others.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling level
The act is ghusl (full body wash). In Hanafi terminology, the ruling level is mustahabb (recommended/sunnah), not fard or wajib.
Mustahabb is synonymous with sunnah in this context.
2
List the occasions and categorize them
Group the occasions into categories: Hajj-related (entering Makkah, Madinah, Muzdalifah, Tawaf), purification after death/blood (washing deceased, cupping), special nights (Bara'ah, Laylat al-Qadr), and extraordinary events (eclipse, rain, fear, darkness, strong wind).
Some occasions have explicit hadith, others rely on analogy.
3
Locate the dalil (evidence) for each occasion
For each category, identify the specific hadith or analogy cited. For example, ghusl after cupping is proven by the hadith of Aisha; ghusl for entering Makkah by the hadith of Ibn Umar.
The text also uses qiyas on the hadith of entering Makkah for other sacred places.
4
Analyze the strength of evidence
Most evidence comes from ahad hadith. Since ahad hadith do not create obligation in Hanafi usul, the ruling is mustahabb, not wajib. The occasions without explicit hadith (eclipse, etc.) are based on general analogy.
This distinguishes the Hanafi position from schools that may consider some of these wajib.
5
Note the Hanafi position and any differing views
The Hanafi school holds all these ghusls as mustahabb. Some other schools may deem them wajib due to different usul principles.
The mufta bihi is the above list.
