ترجمه : (۱۸۲) [۴] پچھنا لگوانے کے بعد [۵] میت کو غسل دینے کے بعد غسل کرے] تشریح : پچھنا لگوانے سے بدن سے خون نکلتا ہے تو ہو سکتا ہے کہ بدن پر خون لگ گیا ہو اس لئے غسل کرنا مستحب ہے۔ اور میت کو نسل دینے کے بعد بھی ہو سکتا ہے کہ اس کا چھینٹا بدن کو لگا ہو اس لئے بھی غسل مستحب ہے۔
صلى الله
وجه : (۱) اس حدیث میں ثبوت ہے. عن عائشة انها حدثته ان النبي علي كان يغتسل من اربع ، من الجنابة و يوم الجمعة و من الحجامة ، وغسل الميت (ابوداود شریف ، باب فی الغسل من غسل میت ، ص ۴۶۲، نمبر ۳۱۶۰) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ حجامت سے اور میت کے غسل دینے سے غسل کرے۔ (۲) عن ابي هريرة أن رسول الله الله قال من غسل الميت فليغتسل ، و من حمله فليتوضأ ۔ (ابوداود شریف، باب فی الغسل من غسل الميت، ص ۴۶۲، نمبر ۱۳۱۶ ترندی شریف ، باب ما جاء في الغسل من فسل المیت ، ص ۲۴۱، نمبر ۹۹۳) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ میت کے غسل دینے سے غسل کرے ترجمه : (۱۸۳) [۲] شب برات میں ۔ [۷] لیلۃ القدر میں ، جب معلوم ہو جائے۔ تشریح : شب برات [ جو پندرویں شعبان کو ہوتی ہے میں غسل کرنا مستحب ہے، اسی طرح اگر معلوم ہو جائے کہ آج لیلتہ القدر ہے تو اس رات کو نسل کرنا مستحب ہے۔
ترجمه : (۱۸۴) [۸] مدینہ طیبہ میں داخل ہونے کے لئے ۔ [9] یوم نحر کی صبح کو مزدلفہ میں ٹھہرنے کے لئے ۔ [10] مکہ معظمہ میں داخل ہونے کے لئے ۔ [11] طواف زیارت کے لئے ۔ [غنسل کرنا مستحب ہے]
تشریح : یہ سب مقامات اہم ہیں اس لئے انکے لئے غسل کرنا مستحب ہے۔ : (۱) مکہ مکرمہ میں داخل ہونے کے لئے غسل کرے اس کے لئے یہ حدیث ہے۔اسی پر سب کو قیاس کر لیں۔ كَانَ ابْنُ عُمَرَ إِذَا دَخَلَ أَدْنَى الْحَرَمِ أَمْسَكَ عَنِ التَّلْبِيَةِ ثُمَّ يَبِيتُ بِذِي طَوَى ثُمَّ يُصَلِّي بِهِ الصُّبْحَ وَيَغْتَسِلُ وَيُحَدِّثُ أَنَّ النَّبِيَّ الله كَانَ يَفْعَلُ ذَلِكَ - ( بخاری شریف ، باب الانتسال عند دخول مکته ، ص ۲۵۵، نمبر ۱۵۷۳ر ترمذی شریف، باب ما جاء فى الانفنسال لدخول مكة ، ص ۲۱۱، نمبر ۸۵۲) (۲) عن ابن عمر قال اغتسل النبي الله لدخول مكة بفخ - ( ترندی شریف ، باب ماجاء فی الاغتسال لدخول مکتہ ، ص ۲۱۱ نمبر ۸۵۲) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ مکہ مکرمہ میں داخل ہونے کے لئے غسل کرے ترجمه : (۱۸۵) [۱۲] سورج گہن ( یا چاند گہن ) کی نماز کے لئے ۔ (۱۳) صلوۃ استسقاء کے لئے ۔ [۱۴] کسی خوف دار شئی ۔ [۱۵] دن کی تاریکی ۔ [۱۶] سخت آندھی کے لئے۔ تشریح : سورج گرہن، چاند گرہن، اللہ کی بہت بڑی نشانی کی چیز ہے اس لئے اس کے لئے بھی غسل کرنا چاہئے ۔ استسقاء کی نماز کسی خوف دار چیز ، دن کی تاریکی ، اورسخت آندھی یہ عذاب کی چیز ہے اس لئے اس کے لئے بھی غسل کرنا چاہئے۔ ۔ حدیث نہیں ملی۔
Section on what ghusl is recommended for: washing the deceased, and on the night of Bara'ah and Laylat al-Qadr if one sees it, and for entering the Prophet's city (Madinah), and for staying at Muzdalifah on the morning of the Day of Nahr, and upon entering Makkah, and for the Tawaf al-Ziyarah. He went to faint? then he regained consciousness and said: Have the people prayed? We said: No, they are waiting for you, O Messenger of Allah. ... From this hadith, after regaining consciousness from fainting, he performed ghusl, indicating that after regaining consciousness from insanity ghusl is mustahabb. (2) There is also evidence in an athar: from al-Hasan who said: when an insane person regains consciousness, he should perform ghusl. ... Translation: (182) [4] After cupping, [5] After washing the deceased, perform ghusl. Explanation: ... Explanation: (1) Evidence in this hadith: from Aisha ... that the Prophet used to perform ghusl from four things: from janabah, Friday, cupping, and washing the deceased. ... (2) From Abu Hurairah ... whoever washes the deceased should perform ghusl. ... Translation: (183) [6] On the night of Bara'ah, [7] On Laylat al-Qadr, when it is known. ... Translation: (184) [8] For entering Madinah, [9] For staying at Muzdalifah on the morning of the Day of Nahr, [10] For entering Makkah, [11] For Tawaf al-Ziyarah. [Ghusl is mustahabb] Explanation: All these are important places, so ghusl is mustahabb for them. (1) For entering Makkah, perform ghusl; there is a hadith for it, and the rest are analogized to it. Ibn Umar used to ... and he narrated that the Prophet did so. ... (2) From Ibn Umar: the Prophet performed ghusl for entering Makkah at Fakh. ... Translation: (185) [12] For the eclipse prayer, [13] For the prayer for rain, [14] For something fearful, [15] For daytime darkness, [16] For a strong wind. Explanation: Solar and lunar eclipses are great signs of Allah, so ghusl should be performed for them. The prayer for rain, something fearful, daytime darkness, and strong wind are matters of punishment, so ghusl should be performed for them. No hadith is found.
Source pages p. 147

Commentary
This passage lists the occasions for which ghusl (ritual bath) is mustahabb (recommended) according to the Hanafi school. It begins by listing the occasions: after washing a deceased person, on the night of Bara'ah (15th Sha'ban), on Laylat al-Qadr if one knows which night it is, when entering Madinah, when staying at Muzdalifah on the morning of the Day of Nahr (10th Dhul Hijjah), when entering Makkah, and for Tawaf al-Ziyarah (the obligatory circumambulation of Hajj). The author then provides hadith evidence for some of these, including a hadith about the Prophet performing ghusl after regaining consciousness from fainting, which is analogized to regaining consciousness from insanity. For cupping and washing the deceased, hadith from Aisha and Abu Hurairah are cited. For entering Makkah, hadith from Ibn Umar are provided. For the last items (eclipse, rain prayer, fear, darkness, strong wind), the author notes that no specific hadith is found, but they are considered important events warranting ghusl. The overall tone is expository, establishing the rulings as mustahabb (recommended) rather than wajib.

Key Terms
غسل (ghusl): Ritual washing of the entire body with water to remove major impurity (janabah) or for recommended occasions.
مستحب (mustahabb): An act the performance of which is rewarded and the omission of which is not sinful; synonym of sunnah in Hanafi terminology.
حجامة (hijamah): Cupping therapy, a bloodletting practice. After hijamah, ghusl is recommended due to the possibility of blood contact.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) After sleeping
B) After cupping (hijamah)
C) Before eating
D) After using the restroom

Key Takeaway
Ghusl is recommended for many occasions; the Hanafi school classifies them as mustahabb due to the level of evidence.

Definition and Evidence for Tayammum
Defines tayammum and provides Quranic and hadith evidence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define tayammum, state its primary Quranic evidence, and identify its conditions according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Tayammum is a wajib substitute for wudu/ghusl using clean earth when water is absent or harmful.

This lesson introduces tayammum, a purified substitute for wudu and ghusl when water is unavailable or its use would be harmful. We begin with the linguistic and legal definition, then examine the primary evidence from the Quran and Sunnah, and finally outline the conditions for its validity.

Guided Path
1
Understand the definition of tayammum
Learn the linguistic meaning (intending) and the legal meaning (using clean earth to wipe face and hands for purification from hadath).
The term 'tayammum' is derived from the root ت-ي-م meaning to intend.
2
Locate the Quranic evidence
Identify the verse (Surah Al-Ma'idah 5:6) that commands tayammum when water is not found.
The verse states: فَتَيَمَّمُوا صَعِيدًا طَيِّبًا
3
Apply the Hanafi principle of amr (command)
The imperative 'فَتَيَمَّمُوا' indicates obligation (wujub) per Hanafi usul, as amr yields wujub unless there is a qarinah indicating otherwise.
This establishes that tayammum is wajib, not merely permissible.
4
Identify the hadith evidence
The hadith from Abu Dharr states that clean earth is the wudu of a Muslim, even for ten years, showing the longevity of the dispensation.
This hadith reinforces that tayammum remains valid as long as water is unavailable.
5
Recognize the conditions for tayammum
Identify the prerequisites: entry of prayer time, inability to use water (due to absence or harm), and use of clean earth.
These conditions ensure that tayammum is only used when genuinely necessary.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب التيمم
ضروری نوٹ: التیمم : تیم کے معنی ارادہ کرنے کے ہیں۔ اور شریعت میں حدث سے پاک ہونے کے لئے مٹی کا ارادہ کرنے کو تیم کہتے ہیں۔ اس کی دلیل یہ آیت ہے۔ و ان كنتم جنبا فاطهروا و ان كنتم مرضى أو على سفر أو جاء أحد منكم من الغائط او لمستم النساء فلم تجدو ماء فتيمموا صعيدا طيبا فامسحوا بوجوهكم وايديكم منه ما يريد الله ليجعل عليكم من حرج و لكن يريد ليطهر كم و ليتم نعمته عليکم لعلکم تشکرون (آیت ۶ سورۃ المائدۃ ۵ ) اس آیت میں ہے کہ پانی پر قدرت نہ ہو تو تیم کرے۔ اس حدیث میں بھی تیم کا ثبوت ہے۔ عن ابی ذر ... قال رسول الله الله الصعيد الطيب وضوء المسلم ولو الى عشر سنين (ابوداؤد شریف، باب الحب یتیم ص ۶۰ نمبر ۳۳۲ ترمذی شریف ، باب ماجاء في التيم للجب اذالم يجد الماء، ص ۳۳، نمبر ۱۲۴) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ پانی نہ ملے تو دس سال تک جنسی تیم کر کے نماز پڑھ سکتا ہے۔
Chapter of Tayammum. Important note: At-tayammum: tayammum literally means 'to intend'. In Shari'ah, it is called 'intending earth' for purification from hadath. Its evidence is this verse: '... and if you are junub, then purify yourselves. But if you are ill or on a journey or one of you comes from the toilet or you have touched women and you do not find water, then perform tayammum with clean earth, wiping your faces and your hands with it. Allah does not intend to make difficulty for you, but intends to purify you and complete His favor upon you that you may be grateful.' (Qur'an 5:6) This verse indicates that if one cannot get water, he should perform tayammum. There is also evidence in this hadith: from Abu Dharr... the Messenger of Allah said: 'Clean earth is the wudu of a Muslim, even if for ten years.' (Abu Dawud, Tirmidhi) This hadith indicates that if water is not found, one may perform tayammum and pray for up to ten years.
Source pages p. 148

Commentary
This passage begins the chapter on tayammum (dry ablution). It first gives a definition: literally, tayammum means 'to intend', and in Islamic law it refers to the act of intending clean earth for the purpose of purification from minor (hadath asghar) or major (hadath akbar) impurity when water is unavailable or its use would be harmful. The author then provides the primary evidence from the Qur'an (Surah Al-Ma'idah, verse 6), which explicitly commands tayammum when water is not found. The verse lists conditions such as illness, travel, coming from the toilet, or having touched women, and then says to perform tayammum with clean earth. The author also cites a hadith from Abu Dharr in which the Prophet states that clean earth is the purification for a Muslim, even if he does not find water for ten years. This establishes that tayammum is a valid substitute for wudu (and ghusl) and is not merely a temporary concession but remains in effect as long as water is unavailable. The Hanafi position is that tayammum is permitted in cases of genuine water scarcity or harm, and it nullifies the state of hadath just as water does, allowing for valid salah and other acts requiring purification.

Key Terms
التيمم (at-tayammum): Linguistically 'intending'; in Shari'ah, the act of using clean earth to wipe the face and hands for purification from hadath when water is unavailable.
صعيد طيب (sa'id tayyib): Clean earth or soil; the material used for tayammum.
حدث (hadath): State of ritual impurity requiring purification; minor (hadath asghar) negated by wudu, major (hadath akbar) by ghusl.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What Quranic verse is cited as primary evidence for tayammum?
A) Surah Al-Baqarah 2:185
B) Surah Al-Ma'idah 5:6
C) Surah An-Nisa 4:43
D) Surah Al-Anfal 8:11

Key Takeaway
Tayammum is a wajib substitute for wudu/ghusl using clean earth when water is absent or harmful, established by the Quran and Sunnah.

Ghusl for Eclipses and Calamities
Ruling on ghusl for natural signs and calamities

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the five occasions for which ghusl is recommended in the Hanafi school and identify the hukm level as sunnah muakkadah.

Core Idea
Ghusl is sunnah for signs of Allah's power and punishment, not obligatory.

The Hanafi school prescribes ghusl (ritual bath) on certain occasions that are considered signs of Allah's might or warnings. This lesson lists those occasions from a classical text and clarifies that the ruling is recommendation, not obligation. The author notes that no specific hadith is found for this ruling, indicating it may be derived from general principles.

Guided Path
1
Identify the hukm level
The text uses 'ghusl karna chahiye' which indicates recommendation (sunnah or mustahabb). Confirm that this is not fard or wajib.
The Hanafi position is sunnah muakkadah.
2
List the five occasions
Extract the five occasions from the text: (1) solar/lunar eclipse, (2) rain-seeking prayer (istisqa'), (3) fearful event, (4) daytime darkness, (5) severe wind.
Memorize these for recollection.
3
Note the author's remark on hadith evidence
The author states 'No hadith found.' This suggests the ruling may be based on qiyas or general principle, not a specific explicit text.
This is an important indicator of authority weight (fatawa mutakhkhirin).
4
Distinguish from obligatory ghusl
Contrast with fard ghusl (e.g., janabah). These occasions are sunnah only; skipping them does not invalidate acts of worship.
A common misunderstanding is to treat them as wajib.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب التيمم (١٨٥) ولصلوة كسوف واستسقاء وفزع و ظلمة وريح شديدة.
ترجمه : (۱۸۵) [۱۲] سورج گہن ( یا چاند گہن ) کی نماز کے لئے ۔ (۱۳) صلوۃ استسقاء کے لئے ۔ [۱۴] کسی خوف دار شئی ۔ [۱۵] دن کی تاریکی ۔ [۱۶] سخت آندھی کے لئے۔ تشریح : سورج گرہن، چاند گرہن، اللہ کی بہت بڑی نشانی کی چیز ہے اس لئے اس کے لئے بھی غسل کرنا چاہئے ۔ استسقاء کی نماز کسی خوف دار چیز ، دن کی تاریکی ، اورسخت آندھی یہ عذاب کی چیز ہے اس لئے اس کے لئے بھی غسل کرنا چاہئے۔ ۔ حدیث نہیں ملی۔
Chapter of Tayammum. (185) And for the prayer of eclipse, and for rain-seeking prayer, and for fear, and for darkness, and for severe wind. Translation: (185) [12] For the eclipse prayer (solar or lunar). [13] For the rain-seeking prayer. [14] For a fearful thing. [15] For daytime darkness. [16] For severe wind. Explanation: Solar eclipse, lunar eclipse are very great signs of Allah, so for these also ghusl should be done. For rain-seeking prayer, a fearful thing, daytime darkness, and severe wind are signs of punishment, so for these also ghusl should be done. No hadith found.

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement. It lists five occasions for which ghusl (ritual bath) is recommended: solar/lunar eclipse, rain-seeking prayer (istisqa'), fear (such as an enemy attack or calamity), darkness during the day, and severe wind. The author classifies these as signs of Allah's power or punishment, and thus ghusl is prescribed. However, the author notes that no specific hadith is found for this ruling, implying it may be based on general principles or qiyas. This is a ruling_statement lesson.

Key Terms
غسل (ghusl): Ritual bath with water flowing over the entire body with intention.
كسوف (kusuf): Solar eclipse; a sign of Allah warranting prayer and ghusl.
استسقاء (istisqa'): Prayer seeking rain during drought.

Ghusl for Entering Makkah: Prophetic Practice
Hadith proof for ghusl before entering Makkah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on ghusl before entering Makkah and identify the hadith proof.

Core Idea
The Prophet's ghusl at Fakh establishes sunnah, not obligation.

This lesson presents the hadith evidence for the recommendation (sunnah) of performing ghusl before entering the holy city of Makkah. The narrations from Ibn Umar and Umar provide clear precedent from the Prophet's practice, which the Hanafi school classifies as sunnah muakkadah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its context
Ghusl before entering Makkah is an act performed by the Prophet ﷺ on his way to the city. Note the location (Fakh) and the time (before entry).
The act is connected to pilgrimage but separate from ihram.
2
Extract the hadith text
Two hadiths are cited: one from Umar describing the Prophet's practice, and one from Ibn Umar directly stating the Prophet performed ghusl at Fakh.
The texts are authentic (Sahih Bukhari and Tirmidhi).
3
Apply Hanafi usul to derive the ruling
According to Hanafi principles, the Prophet's acts of worship indicate recommendation (sunnah) unless there is evidence of obligation. Since no command (amr) is present, and the act is repeated, it is sunnah muakkadah.
The hadith is ahad but its thubut is qati (due to Bukhari), so the ruling is established.
4
Note the ruling level and authority
The Hanafi school classifies this ghusl as sunnah muakkadah based on these narrations.
It is not fard or wajib; it is a recommended purification.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
عمر اذا دخل ادنى الحرم امسك عن التلبية ثم يبيت بذى طوى ثم يصلى به الصبح و يغتسل و يحدث ان النبي الله كان يفعل ذالك - ( بخاری شریف ، باب الانتسال عند دخول مکته ، ص ۲۵۵، نمبر ۱۵۷۳ر ترمذی شریف، باب ما جاء فى الانفنسال لدخول مكة ، ص ۲۱۱، نمبر ۸۵۲) (۲) عن ابن عمر قال اغتسل النبي الله لدخول مكة بفخ - ( ترندی شریف ، باب ماجاء فی الاغتسال لدخول مکتہ ، ص ۲۱۱ نمبر ۸۵۲) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ مکہ مکرمہ میں داخل ہونے کے لئے غسل کرے
Umar: When he entered the lower part of the Haram, he refrained from talbiyah, then spent the night at Dhu Tuwa, then prayed Fajr there, performed ghusl, and reported that the Prophet ﷺ used to do that. (Bukhari, chapter on ghusl when entering Makkah, p. 255, no. 1573; Tirmidhi, chapter on ghusl for entering Makkah, p. 211, no. 852) (2) From Ibn Umar: He said, 'The Prophet ﷺ performed ghusl for entering Makkah at Fakh.' (Tirmidhi, chapter on ghusl for entering Makkah, p. 211, no. 852) This hadith indicates that one should perform ghusl for entering Makkah.
Source pages p. 148

Commentary
This passage provides hadith proofs for the recommendation of ghusl before entering Makkah. Two narrations are cited: one from Umar (may Allah be pleased with him) describing the practice of the Prophet ﷺ, and another from Ibn Umar directly stating that the Prophet ﷺ performed ghusl at Fakh (a place near Makkah) before entry. The Urdu commentary confirms the ruling: ghusl for entering Makkah is established. This is a ruling_with_proof lesson, using explicit Sunnah as dalil.

Key Terms
تلبية (talbiyah): The phrase 'Labbayk Allahumma labbayk' recited by pilgrims during ihram.
فخ (Fakh): A valley or place near Makkah where the Prophet performed ghusl before entry.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

C) It is mubah
D) It is makruh

Key Takeaway
Ghusl before entering Makkah is a sunnah muakkadah established by the Prophet's practice at Fakh.

The Eight Conditions for Valid Tayammum
Listing eight conditions for valid tayammum

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the eight conditions for valid tayammum and explain why intention is the first condition, citing the proofs from Quran and hadith.

Core Idea
Tayammum requires eight conditions; without them it is invalid — intention is the first and critical.

Tayammum is a dry purification allowed when water is unavailable or harmful. It does not clean like water; it is a substitute. The early scholars of Hanafi fiqh enumerated eight conditions that must all be present for tayammum to be valid. This lesson focuses on memorizing these conditions, with special attention to the first condition — intention.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is tayammum, which is a substitute for wudu/ghusl. Its ruling is that it is valid (sahih) when conditions are met.
2
Enumerate the eight conditions
List them: intention, valid excuse, pure earth, wiping entire face and hands, wiping with whole/most hand, striking both hands, absence of hayd/nifas, no barrier.
3
Focus on intention: reality and timing
Intention is 'tying the heart to the action.' Time: at the moment of striking the earth.
4
Prove intention from the sources
The word 'tayammum' means intention; verse commands 'fa-tayammamu' (intend).
5
Note the sub-conditions for intention
For intention to be valid: Muslim, adult, understanding.

Chapter: Regarding Tayammum
Essential Note: At-tayammum: The meaning of tayammum is intention. And in Shari'ah, tayammum is intending clean earth to purify from ritual impurity. Its proof is this verse: 'And if you are in a state of janabah, then purify yourselves. And if you are ill or on a journey or one of you comes from the place of relieving himself or you have touched women and find no water, then perform tayammum with clean earth and wipe your faces and your hands [with it]. Allah does not intend to make difficulty for you, but He intends to purify you and complete His favor upon you that you may be grateful.' (Surah al-Ma'idah 5:6) This verse indicates that if one has no access to water, one should perform tayammum. There is also proof from this hadith: From Abu Dharr... The Messenger of Allah said: 'Clean earth is the purification (wudu') of a Muslim, even if he does not find water for ten years.' (Abu Dawud, chapter on habs yatayammam, p. 60, no. 332; Tirmidhi, chapter on tayammum for the person who does not find water, p. 33, no. 124) This hadith indicates that if water is not available, one can perform tayammum and pray for up to ten years.

(186) It is valid with eight conditions. (187) First: Intention, and its reality is tying the heart to the action. Its time is at the time of striking the hands on the earth.
Conditions for tayammum to be correct: at a glance:
[1] Intention.
[2] There is an excuse that makes tayammum valid, e.g., distance from water.
[3] Tayammum should be on something pure from the earth's species.
[4] The entire area (face and hands) must be wiped.
[5] Wiping of hands and face should be done with the whole hand or most of the hand.
[6] Strike both hands on the earth.
[7] At the time of tayammum, there should be no hindrance like hayd or nifas.
[8] There should be no barrier to wiping, e.g., grease on hands and face.

Explanation: In tayammum, there is no cleanliness like water; rather, it soils the face, however it is a substitute for wudu. Therefore, if the eight conditions are found, tayammum will be valid; if not found, tayammum will not be valid. The details and proofs of the eight conditions are coming ahead. Translation: (187) [1] First is intention, and the meaning of intention is to attach the heart to the action. The time for intention is at the time of striking the hand on the earth. Explanation: Among the eight conditions of tayammum, the first condition is intention. That is, if one intends tayammum and strikes the hand on earth, tayammum will be valid; but if one strikes without intention, tayammum will not be valid. He explains further: intention is the name for intending an action from the heart. And the time for intention is at the moment of striking the hand on earth; if he intends after that, it will not be the intention for tayammum, and tayammum will not be valid.
Proof: (1) The meaning of tayammum itself is intention, so without intention tayammum will not be valid. (2) In the verse: '...then perform tayammum with clean earth' meaning intend clean earth, therefore intention is the first condition in tayammum. Translation: (188) And for the intention to be valid, three conditions exist: [1] Being Muslim. (2) Being an adult. (3) Understanding the intention.

Commentary
This passage begins the chapter on tayammum by defining the term linguistically and legally, then providing the primary proofs: Quran 5:6 and the hadith of Abu Dharr. After establishing the legitimacy of tayammum, the author lists eight conditions for its validity. The first condition is intention (niyyah), which is explained in detail: the reality is 'tying the heart to the action,' and its timing is at the moment of striking the earth. The author gives two proofs for the necessity of intention: (1) the literal meaning of tayammum is 'intention,' (2) the verse commands 'fa-tayammamu' (intend). Then additional conditions for the validity of intention itself are given in (188): being Muslim, adult, and having understanding. This is a ruling_statement lesson with the character of a memorization anchor, as the eight conditions are enumerated for students to learn.

Key Terms
تيمم (tayammum): Linguistically: intention. Legally: using clean earth to wipe face and hands with intention as a substitute for wudu or ghusl when water cannot be used.
نية (niyyah): The heart's resolution to perform an act of worship; the first condition of tayammum.
حدث (hadath): Ritual impurity, either minor (hadath asghar) or major (hadath akbar/janabah).

Eight Conditions for the Validity of Tayammum
Lists eight conditions for tayammum validity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list and explain the eight conditions required for the validity of tayammum according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Tayammum is valid only when all eight conditions are fulfilled: intention, excuse, pure earth, full wipe, whole hand, two strikes, no menstrual/postnatal state, no barrier.

Tayammum is a dry purification method permitted when water is unavailable or harmful. The Hanafi school stipulates eight specific conditions that must all be present for tayammum to be valid. This lesson lists and explains each condition as taught in the classical matn.

Guided Path
1
Memorize the total number of conditions
The matn states that tayammum is valid with eight conditions (shurut). Commit this number to memory.
The number is explicitly given in the Arabic: 'يصح بشروط ثمانية'.
2
List each condition in order
Go through the eight conditions one by one as enumerated in the Urdu text: intention, valid excuse, pure earth, complete wipe, using whole or most hand, two strikes, absence of menstruation/postnatal bleeding, absence of barrier on hands/face.
The text uses numbers 1-8, though the sixth is misprinted as [1].
3
Understand the rationale behind each condition
Each condition serves a legal purpose: intention distinguishes tayammum from casual dusting; the excuse justifies bypassing water; pure earth ensures taharah; full wipe and hand coverage guarantee proper purification; two strikes ensure enough earth; avoiding conflicting states prevents impurity; barriers block direct contact.
These conditions reflect the Hanafi approach to tayammum as a substitute for wudu/ghusl.
4
Apply the conditions in a scenario
Given a scenario (e.g., a sick person without water), check each condition: is intention present? Is water harmful? Is earth pure? Is wiping complete? Are hands fully used? Two strikes done? No menstruation? No grease?
Missing any one condition invalidates the tayammum.

Source Text

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement listing the eight conditions for the validity of tayammum. The author first states that tayammum is valid with eight conditions, then enumerates them in Urdu. The conditions are: (1) intention (niyyah); (2) a valid excuse such as illness or travel; (3) tayammum must be on pure earth; (4) the entire area to be wiped must be covered; (5) wiping must be done with the whole or most of the hand; (6) two strikes on the earth; (7) absence of menstruation or postnatal bleeding; (8) absence of a physical barrier like grease. These conditions must all be present for tayammum to be valid according to the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
تیمم (tayammum): Dry ablution performed with clean earth instead of wudu or ghusl when water is unavailable or harmful.
شروط (shurut): Conditions that must be fulfilled before the act for it to be valid.
عذر (udhr): A valid excuse that permits tayammum, such as illness, lack of water, or travel.

Definition and Timing of Intention in Tayammum
Defines niyyah and its timing for tayammum

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of niyyah in tayammum and identify the correct timing for it.

Core Idea
Intention in tayammum is a heart's resolve at the moment of striking the earth.

In this lesson, we examine the first condition of tayammum: intention (niyyah). The author defines niyyah as a mental determination, not a verbal utterance, and specifies that it must occur at the precise moment of striking the earth. Understanding this ruling is essential because tayammum without intention is invalid according to the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Recognize that niyyah is being defined as a condition (shart) for tayammum. The passage states it is the first of eight conditions.
2
Parse the definition
The definition is 'aqd al-qalb 'ala al-fi'l – the heart's determination upon the action. This is a mental resolve, not a spoken phrase.
Hanafis emphasize intention as an internal act; verbalization is not required.
3
Locate the timing
The text specifies 'waqtuhā 'inda ḍarbi yadihi 'alā mā yatayammamu bihī' – the time is when he strikes his hand on the earth. The intention must coincide with the first strike.
Intention after the strike is invalid; the act must start with intention.
4
Apply the proof
Two proofs are given: (1) Linguistic – tayammum literally means 'to intend', so intention is inherent. (2) Quranic – Surah al-Ma'idah 5:6 'fatayammamū' is interpreted as 'intend clean earth'.
The imperative form indicates obligation in Hanafi usul.
5
Note the consequence
Without intention at the moment of striking, tayammum is not valid. The action must be repeated with proper intention.
This distinguishes tayammum from wudu, where intention is a sunnah according to some Hanafi views.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۱۸۷) الأول النية و حقيقتها عقد القلب على الفعل ووقتها عند ضرب يده على ما يتيمم به. ترجمه : (۱۸۷) [1] پہلی نیت، اور نیت کا معنی ہے کام پر دل کو لگا دینا۔ اور نیت کرنے کا وقت تیم کرنے کی چیز پر اپنے ہاتھ کو مارنے کے وقت نیت کرے۔ تشریح : تیم کی آٹھ شرطوں میں سے پہلی شرط نیت کرنا ہے۔ یعنی تیم کی نیت کر کے مٹی پر ہاتھ مارے گا تو تیم ہوگا ، اور اگر بغیر نیت کے دوضر بہ مارے تو تمیم نہیں ہو گا۔ آگے نیت کا مطلب بتارہے ہیں کہ کسی کام کے کرنے کو دل سے ارادہ کرنے کا نام نیت ہے ، اور جس وقت مٹی پر ہاتھ مار رہا ہو اس وقت نیت کرنے کا وقت ہے، اس کے بعد نیت کرے گا تو تیم کی نیت نہیں ہوگی ، اور نہ تیم ہوگا۔ وجه : (۱) تیم کا معنی ہی ارادہ کرنا ہے اس لئے نیت کے بغیر تمیم نہیں ہو گا۔ (۲) آیت میں ہے فلم تجدوا ماء فتيمموا صعيدا طيبا - ( آیت ۶ سورۃ المائدۃ (۵) کہ پاک مٹی کا ارادہ کرو، اس لئے تیم میں نیت کرنا پہلی شرط ہے۔
(187) The first is intention (niyyah), and its reality is the heart's determination upon the action, and its time is when he strikes his hand on that which he performs tayammum with. Translation: (187) [1] First, intention, and the meaning of intention is to attach the heart to the action. And the time of making intention is when he intends at the time of striking his hand on the thing for tayammum. Explanation: Among the eight conditions of tayammum, the first condition is to make intention. That is, if he makes the intention of tayammum and then strikes his hand on the earth, tayammum will be valid, but if he strikes without intention, tayammum will not be valid. Further, he explains the meaning of intention: the name 'intention' is the heart's resolve to do something, and the time for making intention is when he is striking his hand on the earth. If he makes intention after that, it will not be intention for tayammum, and tayammum will not occur. Reason: (1) The meaning of tayammum itself is to intend, so without intention tayammum will not occur. (2) In the verse it says: 'Falam tajidu ma'an fatayammamu sa'idan tayyiban' (so seek clean earth) meaning intend clean earth, therefore intention is the first condition in tayammum.
Source pages p. 149

Commentary
This passage is a definition and ruling. The author, in the Arabic matn, defines niyyah (intention) as 'the heart's determination upon the action' ('aqd al-qalb 'ala al-fi'l). This is a classic Hanafi definition: intention is not verbal but a mental resolve. The time for this intention is specifically when one strikes the hands on the earth (at the moment of striking). The Urdu commentary elaborates: if one strikes without prior intention, tayammum is invalid. Two proofs are given from the Urdu: (1) linguistic: tayammum literally means intention, so it cannot occur without it; (2) Qur'anic: in Surah al-Ma'idah (5:6), 'fatayammamu' is interpreted as 'intend', thus requiring intention. This ruling is foundational: the intention must be simultaneous with the first action.

Key Terms
نية (niyyah): The heart's determination to perform tayammum, not a verbal utterance.
عقد القلب (aqd al-qalb): The heart's resolve or determination upon an action.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Before starting any action
B) At the time of striking the earth
C) After wiping the face
D) At any time before completing tayammum

Key Takeaway
Intention for tayammum must be a heart's resolve at the exact moment of striking the earth; otherwise, tayammum is invalid.

Three Conditions for Valid Intention in Tayammum
States three conditions for intention in tayammum with proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three conditions for valid intention in tayammum and explain the proof and rationale for each.

Core Idea
Intention in tayammum is valid only if the person is Muslim, discerning, and knows what he intends.

After establishing that intention is obligatory for tayammum, the text now specifies the conditions that the intention itself must fulfill. These three conditions—Islam, tamyiz, and knowledge of the intended act—ensure that the intention is both valid and legally effective. Understanding these conditions helps avoid common invalidations of tayammum.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three conditions
Read the Arabic text and list the three conditions mentioned: Islam, tamyiz, and knowledge of what is intended. Note the Urdu translation uses 'baligh' for tamyiz, but the intended meaning is the age of discernment.
The term 'tamyiz' is technical; don't confuse with puberty.
2
Understand the proof for Islam as a condition
Identify the hadith cited (Abu Dharr) and explain how 'the clean earth is the wudu of a Muslim' implies that a non-Muslim cannot validly perform tayammum. Consider the definition of 'Muslim' and the exclusion of non-Muslims.
The hadith is ahad, but sufficient for Hanafi usul.
3
Understand the rationale for tamyiz and knowledge
Tamyiz is necessary because intention requires conscious understanding; a child below tamyiz cannot truly intend. Knowledge of what is intended is required because one must know what he is doing (tayammum) and its effect (permitting salah). The athar of Sufyan al-Thawri reinforces this.
Knowledge here means basic awareness, not detailed fiqh.
4
Apply the conditions to a hypothetical scenario
Consider a non-Muslim who performs tayammum before embracing Islam. According to the first condition, his tayammum is invalid because he is not Muslim. Similarly, a child below tamyiz or an adult who does not know he is performing tayammum also has invalid intention.
Each condition is independent; missing any one nullifies the intention.

Source Text

(۱۸۸) وشروط صحة النية ثلاثة. الاسلام والتميز والعلم بما ينويه . ترجمه : (۱۸۸) اور نیت صحیح ہونے کے لئے تین شرطیں ہیں۔ [1] مسلمان ہونا (۲) بالغ ہونا۔ (۳) نیت کی سمجھ ہونا ۔ تشریح : نیت کرنے والے میں تین شرطیں ہوں تب تیم کی نیت صحیح ہوگی ۔ [1] مسلمان ہونا [۲] بالغ ہونا۔[۳] نیت کی سمجھ ہونا۔ اگر ان میں سے کوئی ایک نہ ہو تو تمیم نہیں ہوگا۔ وجه : (۱) مسلمان نہ ہو تو کافر کے لئے نہ نماز ہے اور نہ اس کا تیم صحیح ہو گا۔ اس حدیث میں اس کا ثبوت ہے۔ عن ابی ذر ... قال رسول الله لا لا لا اله الصعيد الطيب وضوء المسلم ولو الى عشر سنين (ابوداؤد شریف، باب الحب تیم ، ص ۲۰، نمبر ۳۳۲ / ترمذی شریف ، باب ماجاء فی التیم للجب اذالم يجد الماء، ص ۳۳ نمبر۱۲۴) اس حدیث میں ہے مسلمان کا وضو ہو، جس سے پتہ چلا کہ تمیم کے لئے مسلمان ہو۔ اور نابالغ ہوگا تو اس کے تمیم کا اعتبار نہیں ہے، اور تیم کے مسئلے کا علم ہی نہ ہو تو نیت کیسے کرے گا اس لئے تقسیم کی سمجھ بھی ہونی چاہئے ۔ (۲) اس قول تابعی میں ہے ۔ قال سفيان اذا علمت الرجل التيمم فلا يجز يك ذلك التيمم ان تصلى به الا ان نویت به انك تيمم لنفسك و اذا علمته الوضوء اجزاك ۔( مصنف عبدالرزاق ، باب الرجل يعلم التیم ایجز یه ج اول ص ۱۸۰ نمبر ۸۹۵) اس اثر میں ہے کہ تیم کر رہا ہوں اس کا علم ہو۔ لغت : تمیز : بالغ ہو، اتنا ہوش ہو کہ تیم کیا چیز ہے۔ العلم بماینوی۔ یہ معلوم ہو کہ تیتم کیا چیز ہے، اور اس سے نماز جائز ہوتی ہے۔
(188) And the conditions for the validity of intention are three: Islam, discernment (tamyiz), and knowledge of what he intends. Translation: (188) And for the intention to be correct, there are three conditions: [1] Being Muslim, (2) Being mature (baligh), (3) Understanding of intention. Explanation: For the one making intention, there are three conditions; when they exist, the intention for tayammum will be correct. If any one of them is absent, tayammum will not be valid. Reason: (1) If he is not Muslim, for a disbeliever there is no prayer nor will his tayammum be valid. Evidence from hadith: from Abu Dharr... the Messenger of Allah said: '...The clean earth is the purification of a Muslim, even if he does not find water for ten years.' This hadith shows that tayammum is for a Muslim. And if he is a minor, his tayammum is not considered. And if he has no knowledge of the issue of tayammum, how will he intend? Therefore, understanding of what is intended is also necessary. (2) From the saying of a Tabi'i: Sufyan said: 'If you teach a man tayammum, that tayammum is not sufficient for him to pray with it unless you intend that you are performing tayammum for yourself. And if you teach him wudu, it suffices.' This effect shows that he must know that he is performing tayammum. Lexicon: 'tamyiz' means to be mature, have enough intellect to know what tayammum is. 'Knowledge of what he intends' means he knows what tayammum is and that prayer becomes permissible with it.
Source pages p. 150

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement with support from hadith and athar. After establishing that intention is necessary, the author now lists three conditions that must be met in the person making the intention for it to be valid: (1) Islam: the person must be Muslim, because kufr negates the validity of worship. A hadith is cited: 'Pure earth is the wudu of a Muslim' (Abu Dawud, Tirmidhi). (2) Tamyiz (discernment): the person must have reached an age of understanding (usually around seven years old in Hanafi fiqh) and be sane. A minor who does not understand tayammum cannot have valid intention. (3) Knowledge of what is intended: the person must know that he is performing tayammum and that it permits salah. An athar from Sufyan al-Thawri is quoted indicating that if one merely imitates tayammum without knowing its purpose, it is not valid. The Arabic term 'tamyiz' is glossed in Urdu as 'baligh' (mature) but technically it means having the ability to distinguish (sinn al-tamyiz), which in Hanafi fiqh is typically around seven years, while complete obligation comes at puberty. However, for validity of intention, tamyiz suffices.

Key Terms
تمییز (tamyiz): The age of discernment, usually around seven years, where a child can distinguish between right and wrong and understand basic actions.
العلم بما ينويه (al-'ilm bi-mā yanwīh): Knowledge of what one intends, i.e., knowing that one is performing tayammum and for what purpose.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT a condition for the validity of intention in tayammum according to this passage?
A) Being Muslim
B) Being male
C) Having reached the age of discernment
D) Knowing what tayammum is

Key Takeaway
Intention for tayammum is valid only if the person is Muslim, has reached discernment, and knows what he is doing.

Valid Intentions for Tayammum for Prayer
Ruling specifying valid intentions for tayammum for salah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the three valid intentions for tayammum and distinguish them from insufficient intentions.

Core Idea
Tayammum for prayer requires a specific intention linked to purification or a worship needing purity.

In this lesson, we examine the conditions for the intention (niyyah) when performing tayammum for the purpose of prayer. The Hanafi school requires a specific linkage to purification or worship that necessitates purity, not a general intention of tayammum. Understanding this ensures that your purification is legally effective for the intended act.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is tayammum performed with the aim of praying salah. The ruling is that it is valid only if a specific intention accompanies the tayammum.
2
List the three valid intentions
Memorize the three intentions: (1) intention to become pure (taharah), (2) intention to make prayer permissible (istibahah al-salah), (3) intention for a specific worship that requires purity (ibadah maqsudah).
3
Analyze the two invalid intentions
The passage states two insufficient intentions: (a) intending only tayammum itself, (b) intending it for oral Quran recitation (qira'ah) if not junub. Understand why they are invalid.
4
Apply the rule to examples
Test your understanding with scenarios: e.g., tayammum for tawaf is valid, for reading Quran without janabah is invalid for salah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۱۸۹) ويشترط لصحة نية التيمم للصلوة به احد ثلاثة اشياء . اما نية الطهارة او استباحة الصلوة او نية عبادة مقصودة لا تصح بدون طهارة (۱۹۰ ) . فلا يصلى به اذا نوى التيمم فقط او نواه لقراءة. ترجمه : (۱۸۹) اور تیم سے نماز پڑھنے کے لئے نیت صحیح ہونے کی تین چیزوں میں ایک شرط ہے : [1] یا پاک ہونے کی نیت ہو۔ [۲] یا نماز درست ہونے کی نیت ہو۔ [۳] یا کوئی ایسی عبادت مقصودہ کی نیت ہو جو بلا طہارت صحیح نہ ہوتی ہو۔ تشریح : جس تیم سے نماز پڑھ سکتا ہو، اس کی تین صورتیں بیان کر رہے ہیں، ان تینوں میں سے کوئی ایک نیت ہو تو اس تیم سے نماز پڑھ سکتا ہے، اور ان تینوں میں سے کوئی ایک نیت نہ ہو تو اس تیم سے نماز نہیں پڑھ سکتا ہے۔ [1] پاکی حاصل کرنے کی نیت ہو تو اس سے نماز پڑھ سکتا ہے ۔[۲] نماز پڑھنے کی نیت سے تیتم کرے، [۳] کوئی ایسی عبادت مقصودہ کے لئے تیم کی نیت کرے جو بغیر طہارت کے ادا نہ ہوتی ہو، جیسے طواف کے لئے تیم کرے، یا سجدہ تلاوت کرنے کی نیت سے تیتم کرے تو اس تیم سے نماز پڑھ سکتا ہے، اور قرآن پاک زبانی پڑھنے کے لئے تیم کرے تو اس تیم سے نماز نہیں پڑھ سکتا ہے، کیونکہ زبانی قرآن بغیر وضو کے بھی پڑھ سکتا ہے۔ ترجمه : (۱۹۰) اس لئے اگر صرف تیم کی نیت کی ہو تو اس سے نماز نہیں پڑھ سکتا، یا قرآن کے پڑھنے کی نیت کی ہو اور وہ جنبی نہ ہو تو [ اس تیم سے نماز نہیں پڑھ سکتا ]
(189) And for the validity of the intention of tayammum for prayer through it, one of three things is required: either the intention of purification (taharah), or the permission of prayer (istibahah al-salah), or the intention of a specific act of worship that is not valid without purification. (190) So one cannot pray with it if he intends only tayammum or intends it for recitation (qira'ah). Translation: (189) And for praying with tayammum, for the intention to be correct, one condition from three things: [1] Either have the intention of becoming pure. [2] Or have the intention of making prayer permissible. [3] Or have the intention of some specific worship that is not valid without purification. Explanation: He is describing three situations in which one can pray with tayammum. If any one of these three intentions is present, he can pray with that tayammum. If none of these three intentions is present, he cannot pray with that tayammum. [1] If he intends to obtain purification, he can pray with it. [2] If he performs tayammum with the intention of praying. [3] If he performs tayammum with the intention of a specific worship that cannot be performed without purification, such as performing tayammum for tawaf or for sajdah al-tilawah, then he can pray with that tayammum. But if he performs tayammum for oral recitation of the Quran, he cannot pray with that tayammum, because oral recitation can be done without wudu. Translation: (190) Therefore, if he intends only tayammum, he cannot pray with it, or if he intends for recitation and he is not in a state of major impurity (janabah), then [he cannot pray with that tayammum].
Source pages p. 150

Commentary
This passage is a ruling that specifies the valid intentions for tayammum when one wishes to perform prayer (salah). The author states three valid intentions: (1) intention to achieve purity (taharah), (2) intention to make prayer permissible (istibahah al-salah), (3) intention for a specific act of worship that requires purity, such as tawaf or sajdah al-tilawah. If any of these are present, the tayammum is valid for salah. The Arabic term 'istibahah al-salah' means the permission to enter into prayer; intending this is equivalent to intending the act of prayer itself. The third category covers acts that have a specific purpose. The negative implication (190) clarifies that two intentions are insufficient: (a) intending only the act of tayammum itself without linking it to purification or prayer, and (b) intending it for oral Quran recitation (qira'ah) if one is not in a state of major impurity, because recitation does not require wudu. The Urdu commentary adds that if he intends tayammum for recitation but he is in janabah, then it might be valid? Actually, the text implies it is invalid because recitation is not an act requiring purification. This distinction ensures that tayammum is only valid for purposes that actually require ritual purity.

Key Terms
استباحة الصلاة (istibahah al-salah): The intention to make prayer permissible, i.e., to remove the legal impediment that prevents prayer without purification.
عبادة مقصودة (ibadah maqsudah): A specific act of worship that is intended in itself, such as tawaf or sajdah al-tilawah, which require purity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Intending to recite Quran orally

Key Takeaway
Tayammum for prayer requires a specific intention linked to purification or a worship that demands purity; a mere general intention is insufficient.

Three Conditions for Valid Intention in Tayammum
States the three personal conditions for a valid intention in tayammum.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three conditions for a valid intention in tayammum and explain why each is required according to Hanafi fiqh.

Core Idea
Three conditions must be met for the intention in tayammum to be valid: Islam, discernment, and knowledge.

In this passage, the author presents the three essential conditions (shurut) that make the intention (niyyah) valid in tayammum. Understanding these conditions is crucial because the intention is a fundamental part of tayammum; if any condition is missing, the entire tayammum is invalid. This lesson will walk you through each condition and its evidence from the Sunnah and athar.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Recognise that the passage is about the validity of the intention (niyyah) in tayammum. The ruling is that the intention requires three specific conditions to be valid.
The intention is a prerequisite for tayammum; without a valid intention, tayammum is batil.
2
List the three conditions from the text
The matn states: Islam, discernment (tamyiz), and knowledge of what one intends. The Urdu sharh explains these as being Muslim, being adult (baligh), and having understanding of the intention.
These conditions are personal to the one performing tayammum.
3
Examine the evidence for each condition
For Islam, the hadith 'clean earth is the ablution of a Muslim' is cited. For discernment, the sharh argues that a minor's tayammum is not counted. For knowledge, an athar from Sufyan al-Thawri indicates that one must know he is performing tayammum.
The dalil type is Sunnah_ahad for the hadith, and the athar strengthens the need for knowledge.
4
Note the Hanafi position and cross-madhhab difference
Hanafis require all three conditions strictly. Some other schools (e.g., Malikis) may consider intention valid from a Muslim even without explicit knowledge.
This difference affects the validity of tayammum in certain scenarios.
5
Apply the conditions to a scenario
Given a case, check each condition: Is the person Muslim? Do they have tamyiz (age of understanding)? Do they know that they are doing tayammum for prayer? If any is missing, the intention is invalid.
This step solidifies the practical application.

The conditions for the correctness of intention are three: Islam, discernment, and knowledge of what one intends. Explanation: The person making intention must have three conditions for the intention of tayammum to be valid: [1] Being Muslim, [2] Being adult (discernment), [3] Having understanding of the intention. If any one of these is missing, tayammum is not valid. Proof: (1) If not Muslim, the disbeliever has no prayer and his tayammum is not valid. This is established in the hadith: From Abu Dharr ... the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: '... clean earth is the ablution of a Muslim, even for ten years.' (Abu Dawud, Bab al-Hab al-Tayammum, p. 20, no. 332; Tirmidhi, Bab ma ja'a fi al-tayammum li'l-junub idh lam yajid al-ma', p. 33, no. 124). This hadith indicates that a Muslim's ablution; hence tayammum requires being Muslim. And if one is minor, his tayammum is not considered; and if one has no knowledge of the ruling of tayammum, how can he intend? So understanding is necessary. (2) From the statement of a follower (Sufyan): He said: 'If you teach a man tayammum, his tayammum does not suffice for him to pray with it unless you intend that you are doing tayammum for yourself; and if you teach him ablution, it suffices.' (Musannaf 'Abd al-Razzaq, Bab al-rajul yu'allim al-tayammum a-yujzi'uhu, vol. 1, p. 180, no. 895). This report indicates that one must know he is doing tayammum. Lexicon: Tamyiz (discernment): being adult, having enough sense to know what tayammum is. Al-'Ilm bima yanwih: knowing what tayammum is, and that prayer becomes permissible with it.
Source pages p. 150

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement from the matn listing the three conditions for the validity of the intention in tayammum. The author begins by stating that the conditions for a correct intention (niyyah) are three: Islam (al-Islam), discernment (al-tamyiz), and knowledge of what one intends (al-'ilm bima yanwih). The Urdu sharh explains that the person performing tayammum must be Muslim, adult (baligh, i.e., possessing tamyiz), and must understand what he is doing. If any of these is missing, the tayammum is invalid. The proof for the condition of Islam is the hadith that the earth is a purifier for the Muslim. For discernment, the sharh mentions that a minor's tayammum is not counted. For knowledge, the athar from Sufyan al-Thawri indicates that one must be aware that he is performing tayammum. The Hanafi ruling is clear: these three conditions are prerequisites for the intention, and without them, tayammum is not valid.

Key Terms
التميز (al-tamyiz): Discernment, meaning the person has reached an age of understanding (generally around seven years or above in Hanafi fiqh) and is not a minor lacking comprehension.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
For intention in tayammum to be valid, the person must be Muslim, possess discernment, and know what he intends.

The Three Intentions That Validate Tayammum for Prayer
Specifies three permissible intentions for tayammum to permit prayer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three permissible intentions for tayammum and apply them to determine whether a tayammum permits prayer.

Core Idea
The intention in tayammum must be for an act that requires purification; otherwise, it does not permit prayer.

In this passage, the author specifies the three intentions that make tayammum valid for prayer. The Hanafi school is precise: not every act of worship qualifies. Understanding this distinction is crucial before you perform tayammum and then pray.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three intentions
The passage states: intention of purification, intention to make prayer permissible (istibahah al-salah), or intention for a specific act of worship that requires purity. List them clearly.
Memorize these three as a condition for tayammum to permit prayer.
2
Understand the condition
The tayammum is valid for prayer only if the intention matches one of these three. If the intention is for an act that does not require purity (e.g., reciting Quran when not junub), the tayammum is too light for prayer.
The condition is about the 'purpose' of the tayammum, not just the act of purification.
3
Apply to examples
Work through the given examples: tayammum for tawaf or sajdah al-tilawah qualifies; for reciting Quran from memory does not. Use the rule to test other scenarios (e.g., touching a mushaf, attending a funeral prayer).
The key is whether the intended act absolutely requires purity.

(۱۸۹) ويشترط لصحة نية التيمم للصلوة به احد ثلاثة اشياء . اما نية الطهارة او استباحة الصلوة او نية عبادة مقصودة لا تصح بدون طهارة . تشریح : جس تیم سے نماز پڑھ سکتا ہو، اس کی تین صورتیں بیان کر رہے ہیں، ان تینوں میں سے کوئی ایک نیت ہو تو اس تیم سے نماز پڑھ سکتا ہے، اور ان تینوں میں سے کوئی ایک نیت نہ ہو تو اس تیم سے نماز نہیں پڑھ سکتا ہے۔ [1] پاکی حاصل کرنے کی نیت ہو تو اس سے نماز پڑھ سکتا ہے ۔[۲] نماز پڑھنے کی نیت سے تیتم کرے، [۳] کوئی ایسی عبادت مقصودہ کے لئے تیم کی نیت کرے جو بغیر طہارت کے ادا نہ ہوتی ہو، جیسے طواف کے لئے تیم کرے، یا سجدہ تلاوت کرنے کی نیت سے تیتم کرے تو اس تیم سے نماز پڑھ سکتا ہے، اور قرآن پاک زبانی پڑھنے کے لئے تیم کرے تو اس تیم سے نماز نہیں پڑھ سکتا ہے، کیونکہ زبانی قرآن بغیر وضو کے بھی پڑھ سکتا ہے۔
(189) And for the correctness of the intention of tayammum for prayer with it, one of three things is required: either the intention of purification, or the making permissible of prayer, or the intention of a specific act of worship that is not valid without purification. Explanation: He is stating three cases in which tayammum can be used to pray. If there is any one of these three intentions, one can pray with that tayammum; if none of these three intentions is present, one cannot pray with that tayammum. [1] If one intends to obtain purity, then one can pray with it. [2] If one performs tayammum with the intention of prayer. [3] If one intends tayammum for a specific act of worship that cannot be performed without purification, such as performing tayammum for tawaf, or performing tayammum with the intention of prostrating of recitation, then one can pray with that tayammum. And if one performs tayammum for reciting the Qur'an from memory, then one cannot pray with that tayammum, because the Qur'an can be recited from memory without ablution.
Source pages p. 150

Commentary
This section presents the three intentions that make tayammum valid for prayer. The ruling is that for tayammum to permit prayer, the intention must be one of: (1) purification (raf' al-hadath), (2) making prayer permissible (istibahah al-salah), or (3) a specific act of worship that requires purity (like tawaf or sajdah al-tilawah). If the intention is merely tayammum itself or for an act that does not require purity (like reciting Qur'an when not junub), the tayammum is too light and does not authorize prayer. The sharh gives examples: tayammum for tawaf or prostration of recitation qualifies, while tayammum for reciting from memory does not. The proof for this classification is drawn from the principle that the purpose of tayammum is to fulfill the requirement of purification for acts that demand it; if the act does not require purification, the tayammum is insufficient for prayer.

Key Terms
استباحة الصلوة (istibahah al-salah): Making prayer permissible; i.e., intending to remove the state of ritual impurity to allow prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following intentions would make tayammum valid for prayer?
A) Intending tayammum itself
B) Intending to recite Qur'an from memory when not junub
C) Intending purification
D) Intending to read a book

Key Takeaway
Tayammum permits prayer only if the intention is purification, making prayer permissible, or a specific act of worship that requires purity.

Invalidity of Light Tayammum for Prayer
Ruling on intention-based validity of tayammum for prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi classification of tayammum (light vs. heavy) and apply the rule that only heavy tayammum permits prayer.

Core Idea
Light tayammum suffices for non-worship acts, but prayer requires a heavy intention linked to purification.

This passage clarifies a subtle but essential point in Hanafi taharah: not every tayammum permits prayer. The key lies in the intention (niyyah). The text distinguishes between 'light' tayammum (tayammum khafif) for acts that do not require purity and 'heavy' tayammum for acts that do. Understanding this distinction avoids invalidating one's prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is performing tayammum with only the intention of tayammum itself or for reciting the Qur'an from memory while the person is not junub. The ruling is that this tayammum is invalid for prayer.
The ruling is batil (void) for prayer, though the tayammum itself may be valid for other purposes.
2
Locate the proof (dalil)
The author cites the hadith where the Prophet (peace be upon him) performed tayammum to respond to a greeting while urinating. This shows tayammum for a non-purification act.
Hadith from Abu Dawud.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Since responding to a greeting does not require purity, the Prophet's tayammum was 'light' – not intended for purification. Thus, light tayammum cannot substitute for prayer.
The hadith is zanni in both transmission and meaning, but establishes the principle.
4
Understand the Hanafi taxonomy
The Sharh divides tayammum into three types: (1) for a specific act of worship, (2) for ghusl from janabah (heavy), (3) for a non-specific act (light). Only types (1) and (2) permit prayer.
Type (3) includes reciting Qur'an without janabah, responding to greetings, etc.
5
Apply the principle
For prayer to be valid with tayammum, the intention must be linked to removing hadath (like janabah) or to an act that requires purity (like prayer itself). Light intentions break the validity.
If one was junub and intended ghusl, the tayammum is heavy and prayer is valid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۱۹۰ ) . فلا يصلى به اذا نوى التيمم فقط او نواه لقراء ة القرآن ولم يكن جنبا . تشریح : عبادہ مقصودہ کے لئے تمیم نہیں کیا، اور نہ مطلقا پاک ہونے کے لئے تیم کیا، بلکہ صرف تیم کی نیت کی ، یاز بانی قرآن پڑھنے کے لئے تیم کیا اور وہ پہلے سے جنبی نہیں تھا تو اس تیم سے نماز نہیں پڑھ سکتا ہے، کیونکہ مطلق تیم ہلکا تیتیم ہوتا ہے جو نماز کے لئے کافی نہیں ، اسی طرح قرآن کریم بغیر وضو کے بھی پڑھ سکتا ہے اس لئے اس کے لئے تمیم کرنا ہلکا تیتیم ہے اس لئے اس تیم سے نماز نہیں پڑھ سکتا ہے۔ ہاں جنبی تھا اور جنابت دور کرنے کے لئے غسل کا تیم کیا تو اہم تیم ہوا اس لئے اس تیم سے نماز پڑھ سکتا ہے۔ وجہ : اس حدیث میں حضور علیہ نے سلام کا جواب دینے کے لئے تیتم کیا۔ عن ابن عمر قال مر رجل على النبي صلى الله عليه و هو يبول فسلم عليه فلم يرد عليه قال ابو داود : روی عن ابن عمر و غيره ان النبي صلى الله عليه تيمم ثم رد على الرجل السلام ۔ (ابوداود شریف ، باب فی الرجل برد السلام وھو یبول ؟ ص ۱۴ نمبر ۱۶) سلام کے جواب کے لئے وضو کرنا ضروری نہیں ہے اس لئے یہ تقسیم ہلکے درجے کا ہوا۔ اصول : نماز کے لئے اہم تیم ہونا چاہئے ، ہلکے تیتیم سے نماز نہیں ہوگی ۔ لغت : تیم کی تین قسمیں ہیں [1] عبادہ مقصودہ کے لئے تیتم (۲) غسل کیلئے تیم (۳) عبادہ غیر مقصودہ کے لئے تیم ، جو ہلکا ہوتا ہے
(190) So one cannot pray with it if he intends only tayammum, or he intends it for recitation of the Qur'an while he is not junub. Explanation: He did not perform tayammum for a specific act of worship, nor did he perform tayammum absolutely for purification; rather, he intended only tayammum, or he performed tayammum for reciting the Qur'an from memory while he was not previously junub – then he cannot pray with that tayammum. Because absolute tayammum is a light tayammum that is not sufficient for prayer. Similarly, the Qur'an can be recited without ablution, so performing tayammum for it is a light tayammum; therefore, he cannot pray with that tayammum. However, if he was junub and performed tayammum for ghusl to remove major impurity, then it is a significant tayammum, so he can pray with it. Proof: In this hadith, the Prophet (peace be upon him) performed tayammum to respond to greetings. From Ibn 'Umar: He said, 'A man passed by the Prophet while he was urinating, and greeted him, but he did not respond.' Abu Dawud said: 'It is narrated from Ibn 'Umar and others that the Prophet performed tayammum and then responded to the man's greeting.' (Abu Dawud, Bab al-rajul yaruddu al-salam wa huwa yabool? p. 14, no. 16) Since ablution is not necessary to respond to greetings, this tayammum was of a light degree. Principle: For prayer, a significant tayammum is required; light tayammum does not permit prayer. Lexicon: There are three types of tayammum: [1] Tayammum for a specific act of worship, [2] Tayammum for ghusl, [3] Tayammum for a non-specific act of worship, which is light.
Source pages p. 150

Commentary
This passage rules on the invalidity of tayammum for prayer when the intention is only tayammum itself or for reciting the Qur'an without being junub. The sharh explains that such tayammum is considered 'light' (khafif) and insufficient for prayer. The principle is that tayammum must be 'significant' (muhimm) to permit prayer. The proof is the hadith of the Prophet responding to a greeting after performing tayammum, which is a light act since responding to salam does not require purity. Thus, light tayammum is for non-worship purposes, and prayer requires an intention linked to purification or an act that demands it. The Hanafi position is that only heavy tayammum (for purification or a specific worship) authorizes prayer. If one was junub and did tayammum for ghusl, that is heavy and valid for prayer.

Key Terms
تيمم هلكا / تيمم خفيف (tayammum khafif): Light tayammum performed for an act that does not require purity, such as responding to greetings or reciting Qur'an when not junub.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because it is not performed with earth
B) Because it is considered light tayammum and insufficient
C) Because the person did not face the Qibla
D) Because the person was not Muslim

Key Takeaway
Only tayammum with an intention for purification or a specific worship that requires purity permits prayer; light tayammum for non-worship acts does not.

Second Condition for Tayammum: Valid Excuse (Al-Udhr al-Mubih)
States the second condition for tayammum with proof and example

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition of a valid excuse for tayammum, identify the Hanafi distance threshold of one mile, and cite the Quranic proof.

Core Idea
Tayammum is permitted when using water is impossible due to a valid excuse—hardship is removed.

In the previous lesson, we learned that tayammum requires intention (niyyah). Now we turn to the second condition: the existence of a valid excuse that prevents the use of water. This condition is rooted in the Quranic verse '...and you find no water, then perform tayammum...' (4:43). The Hanafi school specifies that distance, illness, or scarcity constitute valid excuses. In this lesson, we focus on the distance of one mile as a concrete threshold, even if one is within a city.

Guided Path
1
Identify the condition
Locate the second condition in the matn: 'The second: the excuse that permits tayammum.' Understand that this is a prerequisite for the validity of tayammum.
The condition is often summarized as 'udhr (excuse).
2
Study the example given
The matn gives the example of water being a mile away (mil). Recognize that this is the Hanafi threshold for considering water absent.
One mile is approximately 1.6 km.
3
Analyze the proof
The passage cites Quran 4:43 and a hadith from Abu Dharr. Note that the Quranic phrase 'and you find no water' is interpreted by Hanafis to include situations where water is physically distant to the point of hardship.
The hadith emphasizes that earth remains a purifier as long as water is not found.
4
Understand the rationale
The sharh explains that tayammum is a concession to avoid hardship (haraj). Going a mile to fetch water is considered hardship, hence tayammum is permitted even within a city.
This rationale is used to extend the ruling to other excuses like illness.
5
Apply to new scenarios
Use the condition to evaluate other cases: e.g., water scarcity to the point of fearing death, or illness that prevents using water. These also count as valid excuses.
The Hanafi school lists nine examples in the full text.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۱۹۱) الثانى العذر المبيح للتيمم (۱۹۲ ) كبعده ميلا عن ماء ولو في المصر تشریح : تیم جائز ہونے کے لئے دوسری شرط یہ ہے کہ ایسا عذر ہو جس سے پانی استعمال کرنے پر قادر نہ ہو ۔ چاہے پانی سے دوری کی وجہ سے، چاہے مرض کی وجہ سے ،، یا پانی اتنا کم ہے کہ اگر اس کو استعمال کرے گا تو پیاسا مر جائے گا۔ تب تیم جائز ہوگا۔ مصنف نے اس کے لئے ۹ مثالیں دی ہیں۔ وجه : (۱) اس آیت میں ہے کہ پانی نہ پاتا ہوتب تیم کرے۔ فـلـم تـجـدوا ماء فتيـمـمـوا صعيدا طيبا فامسحوا بوجوهكم وايديكم .. ( آیت ۴۳ سورة النساء۴ ) (۲) اس حدیث میں بھی ہے۔ عن ابي ذر عن النبي الله قال : الصعيد الطيب طهور ما لم يوجد الماء و لو الى عشر حجج ، فاذا وجدت الماء فأمسه بشرتك (مصنف ابن ابی شبيبة ، ۱۹۱ الرجل يجنب وليس يقدر على الماء ، ج اول ص ۱۴۴ نمبر (۱۶۶) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ پانی نہ ملے تو تیم کرے۔ ترجمه : (۱۹۲) [1] جیسے پانی سے ایک میل دور ہو، چاہے شہر ہی میں کیوں نہ ہو۔ تشریح : پانی ایک میل دوری پر ہو تو گویا کہ اس نے پانی نہیں پایا اس لئے اس کو تیم کر کے نماز پڑھنے کی اجازت ہے۔ آدمی آبادی میں ہے جسکو مصر کہتے ہیں لیکن ایک میل دوری پر پانی ہے تب بھی تیم کی اجازت ہوگی۔ وجه : (۱) تیم کی آیت میں یہ ہے کہ تیم اس لئے جائز قرار دیا تا کہ عبادت کرنے میں حرج نہ ہو، اور ایک میل جانے میں حرج
(191) The second: the excuse that permits tayammum. (192) Like being a mile away from water, even if in the city. Explanation: The second condition for tayammum to be permissible is that there be an excuse due to which one is unable to use water, whether due to distance from water, or due to illness, or because the water is so little that if he uses it he will die of thirst. Then tayammum is permissible. The author gives nine examples for this. Proof: (1) In this verse it is: '...and you find no water, then perform tayammum with clean earth and wipe your faces and hands...' (Surah al-Nisa 4:43). (2) Also in this hadith: From Abu Dharr from the Prophet (peace be upon him): 'Clean earth is a purifier as long as water is not found, even for ten years; and when you find water, let it touch your skin.' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, Bab al-rajul yajunbu wa laysa yaqdiru 'ala al-ma', vol. 1, p. 144, no. 166). This hadith indicates that if water is not found, perform tayammum. Translation: (192) [1] Like being a mile away from water, even if in the city. Explanation: If water is a mile away, then it is as if he has not found water, so he is permitted to perform tayammum and pray. A person is in a populated area called a city, but if water is a mile away, tayammum is still permitted. Proof: (1) In the verse of tayammum, tayammum is made permissible so that there is no hardship in worship, and going a mile causes hardship.
Source pages p. 151

Commentary
This passage addresses the second condition for tayammum: the existence of a valid excuse (udhr) that prevents the use of water. The matn gives as an example being a mile away from water, even if one is within a city (misr). The sharh explains that the excuse can be distance, illness, or scarcity of water to the point of fearing death. The author mentions nine examples in his work. The proof is from the Quran (4:43) and hadith (from Abu Dharr). The key principle is that tayammum is a concession to avoid hardship. The distance of one mile is considered sufficient hardship to permit tayammum, even within a city. This is the Hanafi position: the threshold for distance is one mile (approximately 1.6 km). If water is within that distance, one must go to it unless there is another excuse.

Key Terms
عذر (udhr): A legitimate excuse that prevents the use of water, such as distance, illness, or scarcity.
ميل (mil): A mile, a unit of distance approximately 1.6 km. The Hanafi threshold for absence of water.
حرج (haraj): Hardship; the rationale for permitting tayammum to remove difficulty in worship.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Being Muslim

Key Takeaway
Tayammum is permissible only when a valid excuse (such as water being one mile away) prevents using water, based on Quran and hadith.

Light vs. Heavy Tayammum: Intention Matters
Explains light tayammum does not suffice for prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between light and heavy tayammum based on intention and state whether a given tayammum is sufficient for prayer.

Core Idea
Intention determines the weight of tayammum; only heavy tayammum suffices for prayer.

Many assume that any tayammum permits prayer. This lesson clarifies that tayammum has grades: a 'light' tayammum performed for a non-obligatory act (like reciting Quran without janabah) does not validate prayer. Only a 'heavy' tayammum intended for worship or removing janabah is sufficient. The Prophet's practice of performing tayammum to answer a greeting illustrates this distinction.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
First, recognize what act is being discussed: performing tayammum with a specific intention. The ruling is that light tayammum does not permit prayer, while heavy tayammum does.
Intention is the dividing factor.
2
Locate the dalil
The hadith from Sunan Abi Dawud: the Prophet performed tayammum to respond to a greeting while urinating. This was a non-obligatory act, showing tayammum for such purposes is light.
The Prophet's act is the proof.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The implication: since responding to a greeting does not require wudu, the tayammum performed for it is not meant for prayer. Therefore, a light tayammum cannot substitute for wudu when prayer is intended.
The absence of wudu necessity indicates the tayammum's weight.
4
Derive the Hanafi principle
The principle: 'For prayer, a heavy tayammum is required; a light tayammum does not suffice.' Heavy tayammum is either for intended worship (e.g., prayer) or for ghusl from janabah.
This is the core legal takeaway.
5
Apply to new scenarios
If someone does tayammum to read Quran while not in janabah, it is light. If they later need to pray, the tayammum is invalid for prayer. Conversely, tayammum for janabah removal is heavy.
Practical test of understanding.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تشریح : عبادہ مقصودہ کے لئے تیمم نہیں کیا، اور نہ مطلقا پاک ہونے کے لئے تیم کیا، بلکہ صرف تیم کی نیت کی ، یاز بانی قرآن پڑھنے کے لئے تیم کیا اور وہ پہلے سے جنبی نہیں تھا تو اس تیم سے نماز نہیں پڑھ سکتا ہے، کیونکہ مطلق تیم ہلکا تیتیم ہوتا ہے جو نماز کے لئے کافی نہیں ، اسی طرح قرآن کریم بغیر وضو کے بھی پڑھ سکتا ہے اس لئے اس کے لئے تمیم کرنا ہلکا تیتیم ہے اس لئے اس تیم سے نماز نہیں پڑھ سکتا ہے۔ ہاں جنبی تھا اور جنابت دور کرنے کے لئے غسل کا تیم کیا تو اہم تیم ہوا اس لئے اس تیم سے نماز پڑھ سکتا ہے۔ وجہ : اس حدیث میں حضور علیہ نے سلام کا جواب دینے کے لئے تیتم کیا۔ عن ابن عمر قال مر رجل على النبي صلى الله عليه و هو يبول فسلم عليه فلم يرد عليه قال ابو داود : روی عن ابن عمر و غيره ان النبي عليه تيمم ثم رد على الرجل السلام ۔ (ابوداود شریف ، باب فی الرجل برد السلام وھو یبول ؟ ص ۱۴ نمبر ۱۶) سلام کے جواب کے لئے وضو کرنا ضروری نہیں ہے اس لئے یہ تقسیم ہلکے درجے کا ہوا۔ اصول : نماز کے لئے اہم تیم ہونا چاہئے ، ہلکے تیتیم سے نماز نہیں ہوگی ۔ لغت : تیم کی تین قسمیں ہیں [1] عبادہ مقصودہ کے لئے تیتم (۲) غسل کیلئے تیم (۳) عبادہ غیر مقصودہ کے لئے تیم ، جو ہلکا ہوتا ہے
Explanation: He did not perform tayammum for an intended worship, nor did he perform tayammum for absolute purification. Rather, he made intention for tayammum or performed tayammum for reciting the Quran and he was not in a state of janabah previously. Then he cannot pray with this tayammum because an absolute tayammum is a light tayammum that is not sufficient for prayer. Similarly, the Quran can be recited without wudu, so performing tayammum for it is a light tayammum; therefore he cannot pray with this tayammum. Yes, if he was in janabah and performed tayammum for ghusl to remove janabah, then it is an important tayammum, so he can pray with it. Evidence: In this hadith, the Prophet (peace be upon him) performed tayammum to respond to the greeting. From Ibn Umar: A man passed by the Prophet while he was urinating and greeted him, but he did not respond. Abu Dawud said: It is narrated from Ibn Umar and others that the Prophet performed tayammum then responded to the man’s greeting. (Abu Dawud, chapter on replying to greeting while urinating, p. 14, no. 16). Wudu is not necessary for responding to a greeting, so this tayammum is of a light level. Principle: For prayer, an important tayammum is required; a light tayammum will not suffice. Lexicon: Tayammum is of three types: [1] Tayammum for intended worship, [2] Tayammum for ghusl, [3] Tayammum for non-intended worship, which is light.
Source pages p. 151

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from hadith. It explains that tayammum is not a single category but has levels of importance depending on the intention. If a person performs tayammum with the intention of being pure in an absolute sense, or for reciting Quran (which does not require wudu), this is a 'light' tayammum that does not suffice for prayer. However, if the tayammum is performed to remove major impurity (janabah) for the purpose of ghusl, it is 'heavy' and valid for prayer. The proof is the incident where the Prophet performed tayammum to respond to a greeting, which is a non-essential act, indicating that such tayammum is light and not intended for prayer. The principle is that prayer requires a heavy tayammum. The three types are: (1) for intended worship (like prayer), (2) for ghusl, (3) for non-intended worship (light).

Key Terms
تیمم (tayammum): Dry ablution with earth as a substitute for wudu or ghusl

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person performs tayammum with the intention of reciting the Quran (while not being in janabah), can they pray with that tayammum?
A) Yes, because tayammum purifies for any act.
B) No, because it is a light tayammum intended for a non-essential act.
C) Yes, if they also intend prayer later.
D) No, because reciting Quran requires wudu.

Key Takeaway
Tayammum has grades; only heavy tayammum (for worship or ghusl) is valid for prayer.

The Second Condition for Tayammum: A Valid Excuse
States the necessity of an excuse preventing water use

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the second condition for tayammum, identify valid excuses, and cite the Quranic and hadith evidence.

Core Idea
Tayammum requires a valid excuse that prevents water use, such as distance, illness, or fear of thirst.

In this lesson, we examine the second condition for tayammum: the existence of an excuse (udhr) that prevents one from using water. The author provides nine examples, including physical absence of water, illness, and risk of dying from thirst. This condition is derived directly from the Quranic command to perform tayammum when water is not found, and is reinforced by the hadith that clean earth is a purifier as long as water is absent.

Guided Path
1
Define the condition
Explain that tayammum is only valid when there is an excuse preventing water use. Note that the excuse can be lack of water, physical inability, or harm from use.
The condition is derived from the Quranic phrase 'lam tajidu ma' (you do not find water).
2
List the examples
The author gives nine examples; the passage mentions three: distance from water, illness, and scarcity of water leading to death from thirst. Recognize that any valid excuse of this type suffices.
These examples cover both absence of water and inability to use it due to harm.
3
Identify the Quranic proof
The verse 4:43 commands tayammum when water is not found. The imperative 'fatyammamu' indicates obligation (wajib), and the condition 'lam tajidu' confirms the necessity of the excuse.
The Quranic evidence is qat'i al-thubut and qat'i al-dalalah.
4
Identify the hadith proof
The hadith of Abu Dhar states that clean earth is a purifier as long as water is not found, even for ten years. This emphasizes that tayammum is a temporary substitute until water is available.
The hadith reinforces the Quranic ruling and extends the duration of excuse.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه : (۱۹۱) [۲] دوسری شرط تیم کو درست کرنے والا عذر ہو۔ تشریح : تیم جائز ہونے کے لئے دوسری شرط یہ ہے کہ ایسا عذر ہو جس سے پانی استعمال کرنے پر قادر نہ ہو ۔ چاہے پانی سے دوری کی وجہ سے، چاہے مرض کی وجہ سے ،، یا پانی اتنا کم ہے کہ اگر اس کو استعمال کرے گا تو پیاسا مر جائے گا۔ تب تیم جائز ہوگا۔ مصنف نے اس کے لئے ۹ مثالیں دی ہیں۔ وجه : (۱) اس آیت میں ہے کہ پانی نہ پاتا ہوتب تیم کرے۔ فـلـم تـجـدوا ماء فتيـمـمـوا صعيدا طيبا فامسحوا بوجوهكم وايديكم .. ( آیت ۴۳ سورة النساء۴ ) (۲) اس حدیث میں بھی ہے۔ عن ابي ذر عن النبي الله قال : الصعيد الطيب طهور ما لم يوجد الماء و لو الى عشر حجج ، فاذا وجدت الماء فأمسه بشرتك (مصنف ابن ابی شبيبة ، ۱۹۱ الرجل يجنب وليس يقدر على الماء ، ج اول ص ۱۴۴ نمبر (۱۶۶) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ پانی نہ ملے تو تیم کرے۔
Translation: (191) [2] The second condition is the excuse that makes tayammum valid. Explanation: For tayammum to be permissible, the second condition is that there be an excuse due to which one is not able to use water, whether due to distance from water, or due to illness, or water is so little that if he uses it he will die of thirst. Then tayammum will be permissible. The author has given 9 examples for it. Evidence: (1) In this verse: 'And if you do not find water, then perform tayammum with clean earth and wipe your faces and hands...' (Surah Nisa, 4:43). (2) Also in this hadith: From Abu Dhar from the Prophet: 'Clean earth is a purifier as long as water is not found, even for ten years; when you find water, then let it touch your skin.' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba, no. 166). This hadith indicates that when water is not found, one should do tayammum.
Source pages p. 151

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from Quran and Sunnah. It states the second condition for tayammum: one must have a valid excuse that prevents use of water. Examples include distance from water, illness, or fear of thirst. The proof includes the Quranic verse commanding tayammum when water is not found, and the hadith from Abu Dhar that clean earth purifies as long as water is absent, even for ten years. The author mentions that there are nine specific examples, which follow in subsequent sections.

Key Terms
عذر (udhr): A legitimate excuse that prevents use of water, such as distance, illness, or fear of thirst
