Chapter of Tayammum. (198) Fourth: covering the entire place of wiping. (199) Fifth: that one wipes with the entire hand or most of it, even... It can be performed with tayammum. Lexicon: turāb: soil, raml: sand, ḥaṭab: wood, fiḍḍah: silver, dhahab: gold. Translation: (198) [4] The fourth condition is that the entire place must be wiped. Explanation: The fourth condition of tayammum is that wherever one needs to wipe, such as the whole face and both hands, the wiping must cover the entire area, not leaving even a hair's breadth; otherwise tayammum is not valid. Merely wiping the palm is insufficient. Evidence: (1) Tayammum is a substitute for wudu, and in wudu washing includes the elbows, not leaving any dry spot; similarly tayammum must include the elbows. (2) This is proven by the hadith of ‘Ammār ibn Yāsir: they were with the Messenger of Allah and wiped with dust for Fajr prayer, struck their palms on the dust, wiped their faces once, then struck again and wiped their arms up to the shoulders and armpits with the inner side of their hands. (Abū Dāwūd, Bāb al-Tayammum, no. 318) (3) Another hadith of ‘Ammār: the Prophet said 'up to the elbows'. (4) A hadith of Yaḥyā ibn Isḥāq: the Prophet showed him how to wipe, striking his palms on the ground, then raising them to his face, then striking again and wiping his forearms inside and out up to the elbows. (Dāraquṭnī, no. 672) Translation: (199) [5] The fifth condition is that one must wipe with the whole hand or most of it; if one wipes with two fingers it is not permissible, even if repeated until coverage is achieved, except for wiping the head. Explanation: One must use the entire palm; wiping the face or hands with two fingers, even if repeated to cover the entire area, does not make tayammum valid. But in wudu, wiping the head with two fingers covering a quarter is valid. Evidence: The hadith of ‘Ammār as above shows wiping with the palms. Translation: (200) [1] The sixth condition is that there be two strikes from the inner part of the palm, even if in one place. Explanation: Some hadith suggest one strike suffices, but the correct view is two strikes, even if in the same place, using the inner palm. Evidence: Hadith of ‘Ammār. (2) Another hadith: they did not gather dust but struck their palms and wiped. (Ibn Mājah, no. 57) (3) Ibn ‘Umar: the Prophet said tayammum is two strikes: one for the face and one for the hands to the elbows. (Dāraquṭnī, no. 674) Lexicon: bāṭin al-kaff: the inner side of the palm. ẓāhir al-kaff: the outer side. Ḍarbah: striking the dust with the intention of tayammum. Translation: (201) And if dust is on the body and one wipes it with the intention of tayammum, it suffices in place of the two strikes. Explanation: If enough dust is on the body or clothing that a finger leaves a mark, then striking it twice with the intention of tayammum makes tayammum valid, because the aim is to wipe the face and hands with dust; here the dust is touched.
Source pages p. 155

Commentary
This passage is an expansion of the matn on the conditions of tayammum in the Hanafi school. The author lists three conditions (fourth to sixth) with proofs from hadith. The fourth condition requires complete coverage of the wiping area (face and hands including elbows), not leaving any spot dry. The fifth condition requires using the entire hand or most of it; wiping with only two fingers is invalid, unlike wiping the head in wudu. The sixth condition requires two strikes of the palms on the earth, even in the same spot, and using the inner palm. An exception is made if dust is already on the body: striking that dust with intention suffices. Each condition is supported by multiple hadith, mainly from ‘Ammār ibn Yāsir and Ibn ‘Umar, establishing the rulings as part of the sunnah. The commentary follows the order of the matn, first stating the condition, then explaining it with reasoning and textual proofs.

Key Terms
ضربة (ḍarbah): A single striking of the palms on the earth with the intention of tayammum.
باطن الكف (bāṭin al-kaff): The inner part of the palm.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the minimum number of strikes required for tayammum?
A) One.
B) Two.
C) Three.
D) Four.

Key Takeaway
Tayammum requires two strikes with the inner palms, one for the face and one for the hands, based on explicit hadith and the relied-upon Hanafi position.

Sixth Condition of Tayammum: Two Strikes with Inner Palms
States the sixth condition of tayammum and the invalidity of wiping with two fingers

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the sixth condition of tayammum and explain why wiping with two fingers is invalid, citing the Hanafi proof from the hadith of Ibn Umar.

Core Idea
Tayammum requires two distinct strikes with the inner palms; using only two fingers invalidates it.

This lesson examines the sixth condition of tayammum: that it must be performed with two strikes using the inner palms. We will see why wiping with two fingers, even if repeated, is insufficient, and how the Hanafi school derives this rule from the Sunnah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its condition
What is being ruled upon? The act is tayammum. The condition is the sixth: that the strikes must be two in number and performed with the inner palms.
2
Understand the error addressed
The text clarifies a common mistake: wiping with only two fingers is impermissible (la yajuz) in tayammum, even if repeated until the entire area is covered. This differs from wiping the head in wudu, where two fingers suffice.
3
Locate the dalil
The author cites several hadith, especially the hadith of Ibn Umar (marfu'): 'al-tayammum darbatan: darbah li'l-wajh wa darbah li'l-yadayn ila al-mirfaqayn' (Tayammum consists of two strikes: one for the face and one for the hands up to the elbows). This is the primary proof.
The hadith is recorded by Darqutni and Bayhaqi.
4
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The explicit wording 'darbatan' (two strikes) is a command; per Hanafi usul, al-amr yufidu al-wujub (the imperative implies obligation). Therefore, two strikes are obligatory for valid tayammum.
5
Note the cross-madhhab dispute
Some schools, like the Shafi'i, consider one strike sufficient. The Hanafi school relies on the explicit hadith and the practice of the Companions to require two strikes.
The practical difference: a Shafi'i may perform tayammum with one strike, while a Hanafi must use two.

This hadith states that wiping is done with the palm. Translation: (200) [1] The sixth condition is that there should be two strikes from the inner palm, even if in one place. Explanation: Some hadith indicate that one strike would suffice, but the correct view is that there should be two strikes, even if both strikes are in one place, and it should be from the inner part of the palm. This hadith states that wiping was done with the inner part of the palm. (2) This hadith also: from Ammar ibn Yasir when they performed tayammum with the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, he commanded the Muslims to strike with their palms the earth without taking any dust, then wipe their faces with one wipe, then return and strike with their palms the clean earth again, then wipe their hands (Ibn Majah, Bab fi al-Tayammum bi-Darbatain, p. 81, no. 57). (3) From Ibn Umar from the Prophet, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, who said: 'Tayammum consists of two strikes: one strike for the face and one strike for the hands up to the elbows' (Darqutni, vol. 1, p. 188, no. 674; Bayhaqi, Bab Kayf al-Tayammum, vol. 1, p. 329, no. 999). This hadith states that there are two strikes for tayammum, and it is also known that one should wipe up to the elbows for the wiping to be valid. Lexicon: The upper part of the palm is called 'zahir al-kaff', and the inner part is called 'batin al-kaff'. 'Darbah' means striking the earth with the hand with the intention of tayammum.
Source pages p. 156

Commentary
This passage is a ruling from the chapter of Tayammum in a Hanafi fiqh handbook. It presents the sixth condition of tayammum: that the strikes must be two in number and performed with the inner palms. It begins by clarifying a common error: wiping with only two fingers is invalid in tayammum, even if repeated until the entire area is covered, unlike the wiping of the head during wudu, where two fingers suffice. The author then states the condition: two strikes with the inner palms, even if both strikes are made on the same spot. The passage then provides evidence from several hadith: first, the practice of the Companions under the Prophet (peace be upon him), who struck twice and wiped their faces and hands; second, explicit hadith from Ibn Umar stating that tayammum consists of two strikes. The Urdu commentary explains that while some hadith might imply one strike suffices, the correct Hanafi position is two strikes. It also defines 'zahir al-kaff' and 'batin al-kaff' for clarity. The overall thrust is that the inner palms are to be used, not the fingers or the backs of the hands, and that two distinct strikes are required.

Key Terms
باطن الكف (batin al-kaff): The inner part of the palm, i.e., the soft side that faces the body when the hand is open.
ضربة (darbah): A single strike of the hands on the earth with the intention of tayammum, not including wiping.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school requires two strikes with the inner palms for tayammum; using only two fingers or one strike invalidates the act.

Existing Dust Substitutes for Two Strikes in Tayammum
States that existing dust can substitute for two strikes of tayammum if sufficient.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on using existing dust for tayammum and identify the condition that makes it valid.

Core Idea
Existing dust on the body can replace the two strikes if sufficient to leave a mark.

Tayammum normally requires two strikes of the hands on pure earth. However, if a person already has dust on their body from prior contact with earth, the Hanafi school recognizes a concession: the existing dust may suffice, sparing the need for a new strike. This lesson unpacks the condition and reasoning behind this ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is performing tayammum using dust already present on the body. The Hanafi ruling is that this is valid and the existing dust stands in place of the two strikes of the hands on earth.
2
Identify the condition for validity
The dust must be sufficient to leave a visible mark when the finger is passed over it. This indicates enough quantity to transfer to the face and arms.
The Urdu commentary emphasizes that the dust must 'leave a mark' – this is the key condition.
3
Understand the procedure
The person wipes the dusty area twice with the intention of tayammum, then passes the dust over the face and hands. The two wipes replace the two strikes on earth.
Even though the dust is already present, the two wiping motions are still performed.
4
Understand the reasoning
The purpose of the strikes is to obtain dust of the same substance as earth. Existing dust on the body is of that same substance and achieves the same goal, so it suffices.
The legal reasoning (ta'lil) is that the dust is from the same genus (jins) as earth.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويقوم مقام الضربتين اصابة التراب بجسده اذا مسحه بنية التيمم. 
ترجمه : (۲۰۱) اور اگر بدن پر مٹی پڑی ہو اور نیت تیم سے اسے مل لیوے تو یہ دوضربے کے قائم مقام ہو جاوے گا۔ تشریح : بدن پر یا کسی چیز پر اتنا غبار ہے کہ اس پر انگلی پھیرنے سے نشان پڑ جاتا ہے، اب اس پر تیم کی نیت سے دومرتبہ ضر بہ لگائے ، اور تیم کر لے تو تیم ہو جائے گا، کیونکہ اصل مقصد یہ ہے کہ مٹی کی جنس پر ہاتھ پھیر کر چہرے اور ہاتھ پر پھیرنا ہے ، اور یہاں غبار جو مٹی کی جنس سے ہے اس پر ضر بہ لگایا اس لئے تیتم ہو جائے گا۔
And the presence of dust on his body stands in place of the two strikes, when he wipes it with the intention of tayammum. Translation: (201) And if there is dust on the body and he rubs it with the intention of tayammum, it will stand in place of the two strikes. Explanation: There is dust on the body or on something that leaves a mark when the finger is passed over it. Then one should run the hand over it twice with the intention of tayammum, and perform tayammum; it will be valid, because the real purpose is to pass the hand over earth and then pass it over the face and hands, and here the dust is of the same substance as earth, so striking it is valid.
Source pages p. 156

Commentary
This passage presents a subsidiary ruling: if a person already has dust on their body (e.g., from working or previous contact with earth), they may use that dust to perform tayammum. The dust must be sufficient to leave a mark when the finger is passed over it. The person then wipes the dust over their face and hands with the intention of tayammum, and this fulfills the requirement of the two strikes. The reasoning is that the substance (dust) is of the same kind as earth, and the object is to transfer dust to the face and hands. The Urdu commentary elaborates that two strokes are still applied over the dusty area, and the tayammum is valid.

Key Terms
يقوم مقام (yaqumu maqam): To stand in place of; to serve as a substitute for.
اصابة التراب بجسده (isabat al-turab bi-jasadihi): The presence of earth/dust on one's body, not intentionally placed but existing.

Key Takeaway
Existing dust on the body can substitute for the two tayammum strikes if it is sufficient to leave a mark.

Conditions for Tayammum: Cessation of Menses, Postpartum, and Janabah
States two conditions of tayammum with explanatory commentary and hadith proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the seventh and eighth conditions for tayammum and apply them to scenarios involving menstruation, postpartum bleeding, and janabah.

Core Idea
Tayammum is invalid during active menstruation or postpartum bleeding, but valid after cessation when water is unavailable.

The seventh condition for tayammum is that the person must be free from the states that contradict purity: menstruation, postpartum bleeding, and major impurity (janabah). This does not mean that those in such states cannot perform tayammum at all; rather, if water is absent, they may perform tayammum to lift the major impurity after the cessation of the blood flow. The eighth condition, attributed to al-Sha'bi, allows using dust found on plants or rocks for tayammum.

Guided Path
1
Identify the conditions
The seventh condition requires cessation of menstruation, postpartum bleeding, and janabah. The eighth condition permits tayammum with dust on plants or rocks.
2
Understand the exceptions
If water is unavailable after cessation of menses/postpartum, tayammum for ghusl is valid. However, if blood remains on the body and water is available, it must be washed first.
3
Examine the proofs
Four hadith provide evidence: Asma on removing menstrual blood, Aisha on washing semen, Abu Huraira on tayammum for menstruating women, and Ammar on tayammum for junub.
4
Apply the condition
Given a scenario, determine if tayammum is valid based on whether the conditions are met and whether water is available for impurity removal.

Source Text

(۲۰۲) السابع انقطاع ما ينافيه من حيض او نفاس او حدث (۲۰۳) الثامن زوال عــن الـشـعـبـي قال يتيمم بالكلأ و الجبل يعنى ما يقع على الجبل من التراب ۔ (مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب الذی لا یسجد ترا با تیم بغیرہ، ج اول ،ص ۱۶۹، نمبر ۸۳۷/مصنف ابن ابی شیبۃ ، باب ما یجزی الرجل فی تیمه ، ج اول ص ۱۴۸، نمبر ۱۷۰۶) اس قول تابعی میں ہے کہ گھاس اور پتھر پر غبار ہو تو اس سے بھی تیمم کیا جاسکتا ہے۔
ترجمه : (۲۰۲) [4] ساتویں شرط یہ ہے کہ تیم کے وقت اس کے منافی حیض و نفاس وحدث نہ ہو۔ تشریح : اور حیض اور نفاس جاری ہو تو اس وقت تیم نہیں کر سکتی ، اور اس کے ختم ہونے کے بعد پانی پر قدرت نہ ہو تو حدث اکبر کا تیم کرسکتی ہے، اور اگر حیض اور نفاس ختم ہو چکا ہے لیکن اس کا خون درہم کی مقدار سے زیادہ جسم پر لگا ہوا ہے اور اس کو پاک کرنے کے لئے پانی ہے تو اس کو پاک کئے بغیر تیم درست نہیں ہوگا ، اور اگر پاک کرنے کے لئے بھی پانی نہیں ہے تو اسی حال میں تیتم کر سکتی ہے۔ یہاں حدث سے مراد حدث اکبر ہے، یعنی جنابت نہ ہو، کیونکہ جنابت ہوگی تو وضو کا تیم نہیں کرسکتا، بلکہ پانی پر قدرت نہ ہونے کی صورت میں جنابت کی نیت سے تیتیم ہے۔ وجه : (۱) حیض کا موقع نہ ہو ، یا بدن پر حیض کا خون نہ ہو اس کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے۔ اسمـاء قـالـت جـائـت امرأة النبي فقالت أرأيت احدانا تحيض في الثوب كيف تصنع ؟ قال تحته ثم تقرصه بالماء و تنضحه و تصلى فيه ۔ ( بخاری، باب غسل الدم، ص ۴۲، نمبر ۲۲۷) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ حیض کا خون بدن پر نہ ہو۔ (۲) جنابت نہ ہو یا بدن پر منی نہ ہو اس کے لئے یہ حدیث ہے۔ عن عائشة قالت كنت اغسل الجنابة من ثوب النبي الله فيخرج الى الصلوة و ان بقع الماء في ثوبه ( بخاری شریف ، باب غسل المنى وفركه فسل ما يصيب من المرأۃ ص۴۲، نمبر ۲۲۹) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ جنابت بھی نہ کپڑے پر ہو اور نہ بدن پر ہو۔ (۳) اور پانی نہ ہو تو حیضہ اور نفساء بھی غسل کے لئے تیتم کرے اس کے لئے یہ حدیث ہے۔عن ابی ھریرة قال جاء اعرابی الی رسول الله الله فقال انا نكون في الرمل وفينا الحائض والجنب والـنـفـسـاء فـيـأتـي علينا اربعة اشهر لا نجد الماء قال عليك بالتراب یعنی التیمم (سن للبیھقی ، باب ماروی فی الحائض والنفساء الكفيهما لتم عند انقطاع الدم اذاعدمتا الماءرج، اول ص۳۳۳ نمبر ۱۰۳۸) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ حیضہ اور نفساء بھی غسل کا تیم کرے گی ۔ (۴) اور جنبی غسل کا تیم کرے اس کے لئے آیت گزری اور حدیث یہ ہے۔الــم تـسـمـع قـول عـمـار لـعــمــر ان رسول الله بعثنى انا وانت فاجنبت فتمعكت بالصعيد فاتينا رسول الله فاخبرناه فقال انما كان يكفيك هكذا و مسح وجهه و كفيه واحدة . (بخاری شریف، باب التیم ضربة ص۵۰ نمبر ۱۳۴۷ مسلم شریف ، باب التیم ج ۱۵۹ نمبر ۸۱۸/۳۶۸ ) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ جنبی کو پانی نہ ملے تو وہ تیم کرے۔
(202) The seventh: cessation of what contradicts it, from menstruation, postpartum bleeding, or major impurity. (203) The eighth: removal [of something] from al-Sha'bi who said: He performs tayammum with herbage and mountain, meaning what falls on the mountain of dust. (Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq, Bab al-Ladhi la yasjud, tayammum bighayrihi, vol. 1, p. 169, no. 837 / Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, Bab ma yujzi al-rajul fi tayammumihi, vol. 1, p. 148, no. 1706) This saying of a Tabi'i indicates that if there is dust on grass and stone, tayammum can be performed with it. Translation: (202) [4] The seventh condition is that at the time of tayammum, there should be no menstruation, postpartum bleeding, or major impurity. Explanation: If menstruation or postpartum bleeding is ongoing, she cannot perform tayammum. After it ends, if she cannot find water, she may perform the major impurity (ghusl) tayammum. But if menstruation or postpartum bleeding has ended but blood more than a dirham's area remains on the body, and she has water to clean it, then tayammum is not valid without cleaning. If she has no water to clean it, she may perform tayammum in that state. Here 'hadath' means major impurity (janabah), because if one is in janabah, he cannot perform tayammum for wudu, but when water is unavailable, he should perform tayammum with the intention of janabah. Evidence: (1) That there should be no menstrual blood on the body; the proof is the hadith of Asma: A woman asked the Prophet about menstrual blood on clothes, and he instructed to rub it and then wash it. (2) No janabah or semen on the body; the proof is the hadith of Aisha washing semen from the Prophet's garment. (3) When water is unavailable, a menstruating or postpartum woman may perform tayammum for ghusl; the proof is the hadith of Abu Huraira: A bedouin asked the Prophet about being in the desert with menstrual, postpartum, and junub people when they don't find water for months; the Prophet said: 'Take to the earth, meaning tayammum.' (4) The junub person may perform tayammum for ghusl; the proof is the hadith of Ammar: The Messenger sent me and you, I became junub and rolled in the earth, then we informed him, and he said: 'It would have sufficed you to do like this,' and wiped his face and hands once.
Source pages p. 157

Commentary
This passage states two conditions (shurut) of tayammum: the seventh and eighth. The seventh condition is that the person must be free from states that invalidate purity: menstruation (hayd), postpartum bleeding (nifas), and major impurity (janabah). However, the commentary clarifies that if these states are present but water is unavailable, tayammum can still be performed specifically to lift the major impurity; for example, a menstruating woman after her period ends can perform tayammum for ghusl if no water. But if blood from menses remains on the body and water is available to wash it off, tayammum is not valid until the impurity is removed. The term 'hadath' here specifically means major impurity (janabah). The eighth condition is a brief statement from al-Sha'bi, which allows tayammum using dust found on plants or rocks. The passage then provides four proofs from hadith: (1) the hadith of Asma about removing menstrual blood from clothes; (2) the hadith of Aisha about washing semen; (3) the hadith of Abu Huraira allowing tayammum for menstruating and postpartum women when water is absent; (4) the hadith of Ammar allowing tayammum for the junub. These show that tayammum can substitute for ghusl when water is unavailable.

Key Terms
حدث (hadath): In this passage, 'hadath' refers specifically to major impurity (janabah), not minor impurity.
انقطاع (inqita'): Cessation; the complete stop of menstrual or postpartum blood flow.
زوال (zawal): Removal or disappearance; here it refers to the removal of dust or the condition of being free from something.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the seventh condition of tayammum, when can a menstruating woman perform tayammum for ghusl?
A) She can perform tayammum at any time during her menstruation.
B) She can perform tayammum only after her period ends and if she does not have water.
C) She can perform tayammum even during menstruation if she is traveling.
D) She cannot perform tayammum until she has bathed with water.

Key Takeaway
The seventh condition for tayammum requires cessation of menses, postpartum, and janabah; after cessation and in absence of water, tayammum for ghusl is permitted.

The Seventh Condition for Tayammum: Absence of Major Impurity
States the seventh condition for valid tayammum with proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the seventh condition for valid tayammum and explain the Hanafi proofs from the Sunnah.

Core Idea
Tayammum is invalid while in hayd, nifas, or janabah; these must cease first.

This lesson covers the seventh condition for the validity of tayammum according to the Hanafi school: the absence of menstruation (hayd), postpartum bleeding (nifas), or major ritual impurity (janabah). We will examine the textual evidence from the hadith and understand why this condition is essential.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Ruling
The act is tayammum. The ruling is that tayammum is only valid if the seventh condition is met.
2
List the Components of the Condition
The condition requires cessation of three states: hayd, nifas, and hadath akbar (janabah).
3
Examine Each Proof
The author cites four hadiths: (1) Asma' on menstrual blood, (2) Aisha on janabah, (3) Abu Hurairah on desert dwellers, (4) Ammar on proper tayammum for the junub. Understand the legal implication of each.
4
Determine the Hanafi Position and Ikhtilaf
The Hanafi school holds this condition strictly; some schools may differ on whether janabah blocks tayammum for wudu. Note the thamarah al-khilaf.
5
Apply to a Practical Scenario
Consider a menstruating woman with no water: she must wait until her period ends before performing tayammum for prayer.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
السابع انقطاع ما ينافيه من حيض أو نفاس أو حدث. 
أما الحيض: فعن أسماء قالت: جاءت امرأة النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم فقالت: أرأيت إحدانا تحيض في الثوب كيف تصنع؟ قال: تحته ثم تقرصه بالماء وتنضحه وتصلي فيه. 
وأما الجنابة: فعن عائشة قالت: كنت أغسل الجنابة من ثوب النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم فيخرج إلى الصلاة وإن بقع الماء في ثوبه. 
وأما الحائض والنفساء إذا عدمتا الماء: فعن أبي هريرة قال: جاء أعرابي إلى رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم فقال: إنا نكون في الرمل وفينا الحائض والجنب والنفساء فيأتي علينا أربعة أشهر لا نجد الماء قال: عليك بالتراب يعني التيمم. 
وأما الجنب: وعن عمار: أن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم بعثني أنا وأنت فأجنبت فتمعكت بالصعيد فأتينا رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم فأخبرناه فقال: إنما كان يكفيك هكذا ومسح وجهه وكفيه واحدة.
Seventh: cessation of what contradicts it from menstruation, postpartum bleeding, or ritual impurity. As for menstruation: on the authority of Asma', she said: A woman came to the Prophet and said: What do you think if one of us has menstruation on her garment, how should she act? He said: Scrape it, then rub it with water, then sprinkle it, and pray in it. As for janabah: on the authority of Aisha, she said: I used to wash janabah from the garment of the Prophet, then he would go out to prayer while traces of water were on his garment. As for the menstruating and postpartum woman when they lack water: on the authority of Abu Hurairah, he said: A bedouin came to the Messenger of Allah and said: We are in the desert, and among us are menstruating, junub, and postpartum women, and four months pass us by without finding water. He said: Use dust, meaning tayammum. As for the junub: on the authority of Ammar: The Messenger of Allah sent me and you, and I became junub and rolled in the dust, then we came to the Messenger of Allah and informed him, and he said: It would have sufficed for you to do like this, and he wiped his face and hands once.
Source pages p. 157

Commentary
This is a ruling with proof from the Hanafi madhhab, specifically the seventh condition for the validity of tayammum: the absence of anything that contradicts it, namely menstruation (hayd), postpartum bleeding (nifas), or major ritual impurity (hadath akbar, i.e., janabah). The condition means that if any of these is present at the time of tayammum, the tayammum is invalid. However, if the bleeding ceases but blood remains on the body in an amount exceeding a dirham, and water is available to wash it, then tayammum is not valid without purification. If water is unavailable, she may perform tayammum. Similarly, a junub person cannot perform tayammum without the intention of janabah. The text provides four proofs: (1) Hadith of Asma' regarding washing menstrual blood from a garment, indicating that blood must be removed. (2) Hadith of Aisha about washing janabah from the Prophet's garment, showing the necessity of removing semen. (3) Hadith of Abu Hurairah explicitly permitting tayammum for the menstruating and postpartum woman when water is absent, implying they must wait until the bleeding stops. (4) Hadith of Ammar instructing the junub to wipe face and hands, establishing that janabah requires its own tayammum. The Hanafi school follows these proofs strictly.

Key Terms
الحيض (al-hayd): Menstrual blood that discharges from the womb, which prevents the validity of tayammum if present.
الجنابة (al-janabah): State of major ritual impurity requiring ghusl, arising from sexual intercourse or emission of semen.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Absence of water
B) Absence of menstruation, postpartum bleeding, or major impurity
C) Presence of clean dust
D) Intention of tayammum

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school requires that at the time of tayammum, the person must be free from menstruation, postpartum bleeding, and major ritual impurity, as proven by authentic hadiths.

The Eighth Condition of Tayammum: Absence of Barriers
States a condition for tayammum with its proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the eighth condition for tayammum and explain its proof from the athar of Aisha.

Core Idea
Barriers on the skin invalidate tayammum—just as henna must be removed for wudu, so must wax and grease for tayammum.

In this lesson, we examine the eighth condition for tayammum: the requirement that the skin be free of any substance that prevents dust from reaching it. The Hanafi school draws this condition from a well-known athar of Aisha, where she commands a woman to remove henna before wudu. The same logic applies to tayammum, as barriers block the essential contact of dust with the skin.

Guided Path
1
Identify the condition
Pinpoint the eighth condition: removal of substances that prevent dust from contacting the skin, like wax, grease, or dried henna.
The term 'zawāl' indicates complete removal.
2
Understand the rationale
Tayammum requires direct contact of dust (turbah) with the skin. Any barrier, even a thin layer, obstructs this contact and thus invalidates the tayammum.
3
Examine the proof
Read the athar of Aisha about a woman with henna performing wudu. The command to 'scrape it off and humble it' shows that barriers must be removed.
The proof is a sahih hadith (Sunan al-Bayhaqi) but is ahad, thus zanni in thubut.
4
Apply the analogy
Since the same barrier principle applies to wudu (water contact) and tayammum (dust contact), Hanafi scholars extend the ruling from water to dust via qiyas.
This is based on the illa of preventing contact with the purifying medium.
5
Note the Hanafi stance
The barrier must be completely removed; mere thinning is insufficient. The ruling is agreed upon (muttafaq alayh) among the schools.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الثامن زوال ما يمنع المسح كشمع وشحم. عن عائشة في المرأة تتوضأ وعليها الخضاب قالت: اسلتيه وأرغميه. قال أبو عبيدة: قولها أرغميه تقول: أهينيه وأرم به عنك.
Eighth: removal of what prevents wiping, like wax and grease. On the authority of Aisha concerning a woman who performs wudu while having khidab (dye) on her, she said: Scrape it off and rub it off. Abu Ubaidah said: Her saying 'arghimihi' means: humiliate it and throw it away from you.
Source pages p. 158

Commentary
This is a ruling with proof for the eighth condition of tayammum: the absence of any substance that prevents dust from reaching the skin, such as wax, grease, or henna (khidab). Just as in wudu, barriers must be removed for water to reach the skin, similarly in tayammum, barriers must be removed for dust to contact the skin. The proof is the athar (report) from Aisha that when a woman performs wudu with henna on her hands, she must scrape it off and remove it, implying that anything preventing water (or dust) from reaching the skin invalidates the purification. Abu Ubaidah explains that 'arghimihi' means to humiliate and remove it. Hanafi fiqh applies the same rule to tayammum.

Key Terms
زوال (zawāl): Removal or absence of a substance that prevents the dust from contacting the skin.
الخضاب (al-khiḍāb): Henna dye used on hands or feet; it is considered a barrier if it prevents water or dust from reaching the skin.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What does the eighth condition of tayammum require?
A) Wiping with clean dust
B) Removal of substances like wax and grease that prevent dust from reaching the skin
C) Using dry earth
D) Performing tayammum before wudu

Key Takeaway
The eighth condition for tayammum requires that the skin be free of any barrier that prevents dust contact, based on the athar of Aisha and qiyas with wudu.

The Cause and Conditions of Tayammum's Obligation
Ruling statement linking tayammum to wudu

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the cause (sabab) and the conditions of obligation (shurut al-wujub) for tayammum and explain that they are identical to those for wudu.

Core Idea
Tayammum shares the same cause and obligation conditions as wudu.

This concise ruling from Thamarat al-Najah draws a critical link between wudu and tayammum. It teaches that the legal framework for when tayammum becomes obligatory (wajib) is not a separate set of rules, but a direct mirror of the well-known conditions for wudu. Understanding this simplifies the fiqh of purification: if you know the conditions for wudu, you know the conditions for tayammum.

Guided Path
1
Recall the conditions of obligation for wudu
The Hanafi school stipulates eight conditions (shurut al-wujub) for wudu: intellect, puberty, Islam, occurrence of hadath, absence of menstruation and postpartum bleeding, arrival of salah time (if intending prayer), availability of sufficient water, and ability to use water. These same eight apply to tayammum.
These are conditions for the obligation (wujub), not validity (sihha).
2
Identify the cause (sabab) for tayammum
The cause that makes tayammum permissible or necessary is the intention to perform an act that requires purification (e.g., salah, touching the mushaf) when water is unavailable or cannot be used without harm.
In Hanafi usul, sabab differs from shart: sabab triggers the ruling, while shart is a prerequisite for the ruling to apply.
3
Apply the principle
Whenever you face a situation where wudu would be obligatory if water were present, tayammum becomes obligatory in its place. The same rules of exemption (e.g., for children, insane) apply.
Memorization anchor: 'Tayammum mirrors wudu in cause and obligation conditions.'

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَسَبَبُهُ وَشَرْطُ وُجُوبِهِ كَمَا ذُكِرَ فِي الْوُضُوءِ.
And its cause and the condition of its obligation are as mentioned in the chapter on wudu.
Source pages p. 158

Commentary
This is a brief ruling statement that the cause (sabab) for tayammum being permissible (mubah) and the conditions for it being obligatory (wajib) are identical to those for wudu, as previously detailed in the wudu section. In Hanafi fiqh, the cause for tayammum being permissible is the intention to perform an act that requires purification, such as salah, when water is unavailable or harmful. The conditions for obligation (wujub) include having intellect (aql), reaching puberty (bulugh), being Muslim (Islam), ability to use sufficient water, occurrence of hadath (minor or major), absence of menstruation and postpartum bleeding, and that the time for salah has arrived (if one intends to pray). These are the same eight conditions listed for wudu. Thus tayammum shares the same legal framework as wudu in terms of when it becomes obligatory.

Key Terms
سبب (sabab): The cause that makes tayammum permissible/necessary; the intention to perform an act requiring purity.
شرط الوجوب (sharṭ al-wujūb): The conditions that must be fulfilled for tayammum to be obligatory; these are identical to those for wudu.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) They are unique to tayammum
B) They are the same as those mentioned for wudu
C) They only apply to the sick
D) They require the presence of dust

Key Takeaway
The cause and obligation conditions for tayammum are a direct reflection of those for wudu; no separate lists are needed.

Pillars of Tayammum: Wiping Face and Hands
States the two pillars of tayammum with direct Quranic proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two pillars of tayammum and identify the Quranic evidence that establishes them.

Core Idea
Tayammum has only two pillars: wiping the face and hands, based on Allah's command in Surah al-Ma'idah.

The text concisely defines the two essential acts of tayammum. While wudu has four obligatory acts, tayammum is a substitute purification that is deliberately simplified. The Quranic verse cited directly commands these two actions, making them the core of tayammum.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its pillars
Recognize that the passage defines tayammum's two pillars: wiping the face and hands. These are the only obligatory acts for tayammum in the Hanafi school.
The text explicitly says 'its two pillars are wiping the hands and the face.'
2
Locate the Quranic dalil
Find the proof: the Quranic verse from Surah al-Ma'idah (5:6): 'فَامْسَحُوا بِوُجُوهِكُمْ وَأَيْدِيكُمْ مِنْهُ' (So wipe your faces and your hands with it).
This verse is the primary textual evidence.
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
Understand how the verse proves obligation: the imperative 'amsahu' indicates obligation (wujub) in Hanafi usul. The words 'wujuhakum' and 'aydikum' limit the wiping to face and hands. 'Minhu' specifies that the wiping is done with the dust (tayammum).
The verse does not mention wiping the head or feet, so they are not required.
4
Confirm the scope from sunnah
The Quranic term 'aydikum' (hands) is interpreted by the sunnah to include the elbows. Similarly, the face includes from the hairline to under the chin and between the ears.
This is the relied-upon Hanafi position.
5
Note the consensus
Recognize that all major schools agree on the two pillars of tayammum (face and hands), though they may differ on the exact extent of the hands.
The Hanafi view includes the elbows; Shafi'i excludes them.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَرُكْنَاهُ مَسْحُ الْيَدَيْنِ وَالْوَجْهِ. فَامْسَحُوا بِوُجُوهِكُمْ وَأَيْدِيكُمْ مِنْهُ.
And its two pillars are wiping the hands and the face. 'Wipe your faces and your hands with it.'
Source pages p. 158

Commentary
This is a ruling with proof defining the two pillars (arkan) of tayammum: wiping the entire face and wiping both hands including the elbows. The Hanafi school holds that tayammum consists of only two obligatory acts, unlike wudu which has four. The proof is the Quranic verse from Surah al-Ma'idah (5:6): 'So wipe your faces and your hands with it.' The word 'from it' (minhu) indicates that the wiping is done with the dust (tayammum). The Hanafi interpretation is that the face and hands are the only parts that require wiping. The verse does not mention wiping the arms beyond the elbows, but the sunnah clarifies that elbows are included. The text mentions only wajh and yadayn, but the commentary in the Urdu portion specifies that hands include up to the elbows. This is the relied-upon position.

Key Terms
الركن (al-rukn): A pillar or integral part of tayammum; its omission invalidates the act.
مسح الوجه (masḥ al-wajh): Wiping the entire face with dust as an obligatory act of tayammum.
مسح اليدين (masḥ al-yadayn): Wiping both hands including the elbows with dust.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Four, like wudu
B) Three: face, hands, and feet
C) Two: face and hands
D) One: wiping the face only

Key Takeaway
Tayammum has only two obligatory actions: wiping the face and hands, as commanded in Surah al-Ma'idah.

Conditions and Impediments of Tayammum
Stating the impediments, cause, and conditions of tayammum

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the impediments to tayammum and list the eight conditions that make tayammum obligatory.

Core Idea
Tayammum requires removing any barrier to earth contact, just as wudu requires removing barriers to water.

Tayammum is a dry substitute for wudu, so its rules closely follow wudu. This lesson explains the specific condition that no barrier (like wax or fat) should prevent earth from reaching the skin, and how the cause and conditions of obligation are identical to those of wudu.

Guided Path
1
Identify the impediment condition
Recognize that the eighth condition for tayammum is that there must be no substance (e.g., wax, fat) blocking earth from the skin.
This mirrors the condition in wudu for water contact.
2
Understand the proof by analogy
Trace the proof: the hadith of Aisha (ra) shows that khidhab (henna) must be removed for wudu; by qiyas, any barrier must be removed for tayammum.
The proof is from Sunan al-Bayhaqi, a hadith of ahad, but accepted by Hanafis.
3
Recognize the sabab (cause) of tayammum
The cause that makes tayammum permissible (mubah) is intending an act that requires purity, such as salah.
Same as the cause for wudu being mubah.
4
List the eight conditions for wujub
State the eight conditions: sanity, maturity, Islam, ability to use water, hadath, not in menstruation, not in postpartum, and narrow time.
These are all required for tayammum to become obligatory.

Source Text

باب التيمم ما يمنع المسح كشمع و شحم . (۲۰۴) وسببه و شروط وجوبه كما ذكر في الوضوء. ترجمه : (۲۰۳) [۸] آٹھویں شرط مسح کا مانع نہ ہو، مثلا موم یا چربی جسم پر نہ ہو۔ تشریح : جس طرح وضو کی شرط تھی کہ جہاں جہاں دھونا ہے وہاں موم یا چربی وغیرہ نہ ہو، اسی طرح تیم میں بھی ہے کہ جہاں جہاں پونچھنا ہے وہاں مٹی لگنے کے مانع نہ ہو۔ وجه : (۱) اس اثر میں اس کی صراحت ہے۔ عن عائشة فـي الـمـرأة تتوضأ و عليها الخضاب قالت اسلتيه و ارغميه . قال ابو عبيدة : قولها ارغميه تقول اهينیه و ارمی به عنک (سنن بیہقی ، باب نزع الخضاب عند الوضوء اذا کان میمنع الماء ، ج اول ص ۱۲۵ نمبر ۳۶۴) اس اثر میں ہے کہ خضاب ہو تو اس کو دور کر دینا چاہئے تا کہ پانی کھال تک پہنچ جائے۔ ترجمه : (۲۰۴) تیم کا سبب اور تیم کے واجب ہونے کی شرطیں جو وضو میں ذکر کی گئیں ہیں وہی یہاں بھی ہیں۔ تشریح : فصل فی الوضوء مسئلہ نمبر 49 میں، وضو مباح ہونے کا سبب یہ بیان کیا ہے کہ ایسا کام کرنا چاہے جو وضو کے بغیر نہ ہوسکتا ہو تو یہ کام وضو کے مباح ہونے کا سبب ہے، مثلا نماز پڑھنا چاہتا ہو جو وضو کے بغیر نہیں ہوسکتی تو نماز وضو کے مباح ہونے کا سبب ہے ۔ اسی طرح یہ کام تیم کے مباح ہونے کا سبب بنے گا۔ اور وضو واجب ہونے کے لئے آٹھ شرطیں بیان کی گئیں ہیں [1] عقل ہونا [۲] بالغ ہونا [۳] مسلمان ہونا [۴] کافی پانی کے استعمال پر قدرت ہونا [۵] حدث کا پایا جانا [1] حیض نہ ہونا [۷] نفاس نہ ہونا [۸] وقت تنگ ہو۔ تیم واجب ہونے کے لئے یہ شرطیں یہاں بھی ہیں۔
Chapter of Tayammum. What prevents wiping (mas-h) like wax and fat. (204) Its cause and conditions of obligation are as mentioned in wudu. Translation of (203): [8] The eighth condition: there should be no impediment to wiping, for example, wax or fat should not be on the body. Explanation: Just as in wudu it was a condition that wherever washing is required, there should be no wax or fat, similarly in tayammum, wherever wiping is required, there should be no impediment to the earth contacting. Proof: (1) This is explicit in this athar: From 'A'ishah regarding a woman performing wudu while having khidhab (henna) on her, she said: 'Remove it and humiliate it.' Abu 'Ubaydah said: Her statement 'arghimih' means 'disgrace it and cast it away from you.' (Sunan al-Bayhaqi, Chapter on removing khidhab during wudu when it prevents water, vol. 1, p. 125, no. 364). In this athar, if there is khidhab, it should be removed so that water reaches the skin. Translation of (204): The cause of tayammum and the conditions for its obligation are the same as those mentioned in wudu. Explanation: In the chapter on wudu, issue no. 49, the cause for wudu being permissible (mubah) is that one intends to do something that cannot be done without wudu, for example, if one wants to pray, which is not possible without wudu, then prayer is the cause for wudu being permissible. Similarly, this action will be the cause for tayammum being permissible. And for wudu to be obligatory, eight conditions were mentioned: [1] being sane, [2] being mature, [3] being Muslim, [4] having the ability to use sufficient water, [5] occurrence of hadath, [6] not being in menstruation, [7] not being in postpartum bleeding, [8] the time being narrow (i.e., not having enough time). For tayammum to be obligatory, these same conditions apply here.
Source pages p. 158

Commentary
This passage deals with the conditions and impediments of tayammum. The author first states what prevents the mas-h (wiping): any substance that forms a barrier between the earth and the skin, like wax or fat. This is the eighth condition (as referenced from wudu). The proof is taken from the hadith of Aisha (ra) regarding removing khidhab before wudu, analogically applied to tayammum. Then the sabab (cause) of tayammum being permissible (mubah) is the same as for wudu: intending an act that requires purity, like prayer. The conditions (shurut) for tayammum becoming wajib (obligatory) are also the same eight conditions as for wudu: sanity, maturity, Islam, ability to use water, presence of hadath, not being in menstruation or postpartum, and the time being narrow. Note: The Hanafi school considers that tayammum is a substitute for wudu, so its rules follow wudu closely.

Key Terms
تيمم (tayammum): Dry ablution using pure earth as a substitute for wudu or ghusl when water is unavailable or harmful.
مسح (mas-h): Wiping the body part with earth in tayammum.
سبب (sabab): The cause that makes tayammum permissible (mubah), such as intending an act requiring purity.
شرط (shart): Condition for tayammum to be obligatory, such as sanity, maturity, etc.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the eighth condition for tayammum mentioned in the passage?
A) Being male
B) Having no barrier to earth contact
C) Having water available
D) Being in a state of janabah

Key Takeaway
The eight conditions for tayammum mirror those of wudu, and any barrier to earth contact must be removed.
